The Vatican Decides Not to Recognize the Puppet State; Missions in the Northeast Are Still Under the Control of the General Assembly Headquarters; Contacting the Puppet Government on Religious Affairs Has No Political Significance 27

Due to inconvenient transportation between the Roman Catholic capital and "Manchukuo" and the Chinese headquarters, various missions in the puppet state may temporarily enjoy a certain degree of autonomy. However, in reality, the various missions are still under the control of the General Assembly headquarters in China and the bishops stationed in the Northeast. These bishops are only temporarily representing the missions in their personal capacity to contact the "Manchukuo" government on religious affairs. This is only for the convenience of religious administration and has no political significance. It should not be considered that the Vatican intends to recognize "Manchukuo." (18th, Havas)

British Advisor to the Economic Commission Discusses the Situation in China; Domestic Affairs Have Made Great Progress; Economic Construction is Underway 28

(London) Sir Arthur Salter, financial advisor to the National Economic Council of China, arrived here today and will go to Oxford to take up a position as a professor of political science. He made a statement on the situation in China, saying that domestic affairs have made great progress. Except for Sichuan, the infighting among warlords has stopped. Salter also briefly described the recent war in the Northwest, continuing that the National Government has been exercising reasonably effective power in various parts of China. There is a general and very firm desire in the country to eliminate civil war. From an economic point of view, the economic situation is slightly worse than when he toured China three years ago. This is due to the devaluation of the pound sterling, the rupee, and the Japanese yen from the gold standard, and the rising price of silver compared to foreign currencies, which has led to lower prices. However, economic construction in China is currently underway, such as the construction of highways, which the National Government deeply understands its importance. There has been some development in China's light industry, and if the current relatively stable political situation remains unchanged, significant development can be expected, especially in industries related to foreigners. Salter continued to talk about China's railways, saying that the future is quite promising, but there are causes for concern. Salter finally told the Reuters interviewer that he had written a long report, which would be published in both Chinese and English shortly. Salter has been a member of the British Economic Advisory Council since 1922, graduated from Oxford, and served as the head of the Economic and Financial Section of the League of Nations and the Secretary-General of the Reparations Commission. (18th, Reuters)

Obstacles to Naval Conference; Britain, the United States, and Japan Have Different Policies; Hope to Hold Preliminary Negotiations First 30

(Washington) According to senior naval circles today, Japan's demand for naval parity and Britain's rush to build small warships are the biggest obstacles to the future of the 1935 Naval Disarmament Conference. The Navy Department is holding talks on a shipbuilding plan based on the Vinson-Trammell Act's most favorable naval provisions. The above views were expressed during the talks. The talks decided to build smaller warships, destroyers, and submarines first, pending the results of the 1935 Naval Conference. The United States has now decided to reject Britain's proposal to reduce 40,000-ton dreadnoughts to 25,000 tons. Because of the strength of the British naval power and the suitability of its naval bases, this move would not affect Britain, but it is not the same for the United States. Because the U.S. naval power is not sufficient to patrol the defense line from Alaska through Hawaii to Panama, and the U.S. fortresses in the Pacific are the three places mentioned above. However, naval officials believe that the above problems can be resolved if the two countries can hold preliminary negotiations before the naval conference. Britain and Japan have both indicated their willingness to begin preliminary negotiations at any time, and naval experts from the three countries are already preparing. It is said that if the government's public works expenditure appropriation plan can be passed by Congress, the Navy Department intends to request an appropriation of $350,000,000 to build 20 destroyers and 10 submarines. If the plan is rejected by Congress, the Navy Department can lower its desires and only request $200,000,000. The Navy Department does not want to build or renovate its large battleships before the 1935 Naval Conference, because the United States firmly believes that in the future naval conference, regardless of how the ratio problem is resolved, it will strive to stipulate the size of the ships. On this important issue, Britain and Japan may unanimously oppose the United States. Japan naturally supports the construction of small ships, because this move saves expenses and avoids long-distance attacks by Britain and the United States. As for Britain's approval, it is easier to patrol its widespread naval bases if the ships are smaller and the number is greater. (18th, Guomin Dian)

France Rejects British Plan, Universal Disarmament Almost Hopeless; European Countries Are Uneasy and Wary; Italian Undersecretary of State to Visit London Next Week, Attempting a Final Rescue; Limited Disarmament is Better Than Nothing 33

(London) Since the British government issued an important white paper last night detailing the failure of disarmament negotiations, European countries are all uneasy and wary, and are preparing their military forces to await the arrival of the next great war. Universal disarmament is now almost hopeless. In addition to recalling Britain's efforts for the peace movement, the white paper also contains a disappointing note issued by the French government yesterday, namely, France insists on not allowing Germany to rearm, in other words, to implement the suspension of disarmament negotiations. After Lord Privy Seal Eden's tour of Europe, the documents exchanged between various countries regarding the British disarmament plan are all included in this white paper. (19th, Guomin Dian)

(London) Italian Undersecretary of State Suvich will arrive here from Rome early next week, intending to make a last-minute attempt to salvage the current situation of disarmament. It is heard that Suvich's intention is that even limited disarmament is better than no disarmament. Suvich does not want to pursue the claims in Italian Prime Minister Mussolini's plan, but believes that if the British plan can be accepted by the public, it is worthy of Italy's full support. (19th, Reuters)

(Rome) People here regard France's rejection of the British disarmament plan as a natural consequence of Britain's refusal to guarantee that it would not assist France in the event of a German attack on France. However, Italy hopes that disarmament talks will continue, because Italy is even more convinced that the memorandum issued by Italian Prime Minister Mussolini in January can eventually serve as the basis for future talks between the four great powers. The Italian Prime Minister's memorandum expresses doubt about whether an agreement can be reached on not allowing Germany to dispose of armaments, and the question is how to prevent the disposal of armaments from exceeding the scope of the agreement. According to this memorandum, the Italian government believes that if there are conditions that can satisfy the public opinion of all countries, a convention can be concluded, and this convention should contain the following articles: (1) Abolish chemical warfare, (2) Prohibit the bombing of civilians, (3) Limit the military spending of countries not bound by the treaty according to the existing standards, (4) Limit the land armaments of countries not bound by the treaty according to the existing standards. People here now claim that the Italian Prime Minister is prepared to accept suggestions and amendments, as long as the basic principles of his memorandum are accepted. (18th, Reuters)

Mediation Ends in Failure, Britain Issues White Paper 34

(London) The British authorities issued a white paper tonight, containing various official documents exchanged between Britain and other governments during the negotiations in the past two months. The most noteworthy of these is Germany's explanation on April 16 of its views on the British disarmament memorandum. It stated that Germany was prepared to accept the British disarmament memorandum as the basis for a convention with certain important amendments, and stated that Germany could not wait two years for a suitable method of air defense. Therefore, at the beginning of the convention, it was willing to have a short-range machine gun squadron for national defense, but bombers were not included. Germany agreed that its air force would not exceed 30% of the combined air force of neighboring countries, or 50% of the number of French military aircraft. Germany is willing to maintain this position in the first five years of the convention, but after five years, there must be increases or decreases, so that when the ten-year term of the convention expires, Germany can reach the same level as the major air powers. Germany is also prepared to agree to manage the storm troopers and other organizations on a reciprocal basis, so that their non-military nature can be proven by other countries' supervision. This management regulation must include the following provisions: these groups must not possess military equipment, must not receive military training, and must not be commanded by formal officers. Germany is also prepared to agree to other countries' disarmament being postponed until the end of the fifth year. According to the disarmament measures stipulated in the British memorandum, they would be implemented five years after the regulations have been stipulated. Germany also accepted other proposals in the British memorandum regarding supervision. Germany also continues to recognize the Treaty of Locarno. Germany believes that re-entering the League of Nations can only be handled after the disarmament issue, especially the issue of Germany's equal rights, is resolved. (18th, Reuters)

(London) The cabinet has decided to publish the documents recently exchanged between various countries on the issue of disarmament in a white paper. The general interpretation of this matter is that the cabinet's intention in publishing the white paper is to indicate that the negotiations centered on the MacDonald Disarmament Plan have now come to an end. From now on, the disarmament issue will be discussed in Geneva. Political circles are not very surprised by the French reply. Generally speaking, members of parliament show a hint of worry as the future seems uncertain. (17th, Havas)

The Process of Anglo-French Negotiations on Guarantee Issues in the Treaty of Disarmament 35

(Paris) The French government's explanation of the implementation guarantee issue of the Disarmament Treaty, and its response to the British government's official document, was briefly reported yesterday by telegraph. Here are additional details on the recent exchange of documents between Britain and France regarding the disarmament issue, with aspects not previously covered in detail by earlier telegrams. After receiving the French government's response on March 17th this year, the British government sent a formal document to the French government on March 28th, raising several questions regarding the "guarantee" mentioned in the French response, requesting clarification. The next day, the British Ambassador to France, Lord Tyrrell, also raised three questions to the French Foreign Ministry: (1) reduction of France's own armaments, (2) benefits granted to Germany in the British plan, and (3) guarantees for the implementation of the Disarmament Treaty.

After receiving the British questions, the French government sent a verbal note to the British government on April 6th, briefly responding to the British questions. Yesterday afternoon, it prepared a formal document explaining France's views. In fact, after the French sent the verbal note on April 6th and before sending the formal document yesterday, the British government had also sent a note to the French government, raising two questions. This note was delivered to the French Ambassador to the UK, Corbin, by the British Foreign Office on April 10th, requesting him to forward it. The content included two questions:

(1) Regarding the possibility of establishing an agreement on guarantees for the implementation of the Disarmament Treaty, is the French government prepared to accept the British memorandum on disarmament of January 31st this year? (Note: The main idea of the British memorandum of January 31st is that European countries must choose one of the following two paths: (1) Negotiate a treaty to have the most heavily armed countries abolish certain types of weapons; (2) If the most heavily armed countries cannot follow the first option, then a treaty should be established based on existing armaments, limiting any further increases. However, the British government wants to actively pursue the first method.)

(2) If France gives an affirmative answer to the first question, then please precisely explain what kind of guarantees France hopes to adopt for the implementation of the Disarmament Treaty.

The British note finally requested a swift response from France. After receiving this note, the French Foreign Minister supervised the drafting of a formal document by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs staff and had it reviewed by administrative and military experts with prestige. It was then delivered to the British government yesterday afternoon, which is the content reported in our telegram yesterday. (Havas dispatch, 18th)

The East Asian Neighbor's Military Buildup Threatens French Security; Germany's Return to Geneva Can Alleviate This Worry 36

(London) Government officials secretly discussed this morning in the office of the Lord Privy Seal, Anthony Eden, the French note refusing the British disarmament plan. Eden has been a "salesman" for the British disarmament plan in recent times.

The French note is a response to the British note of April 10th. The British note asked (1) whether France is willing to accept the British memorandum, revised according to the suggestions made by German Chancellor Hitler to Eden, as the basis for the disarmament treaty, and (2) if willing to accept, what guarantees France requires.

The French reply asks the UK to pay attention to Germany's increase of 352 million marks in its land, sea and air force budgets, saying that this is proof that the German government is violating treaties and promoting rearmament in various ways to a degree that it deems appropriate. Germany's neighboring countries cannot ignore the imminent danger. In particular, many airfields have been illegally equipped in areas where military facilities are prohibited. At the same time, the German government would rather complete its paramilitary organizations for war purposes than abolish them or convert them to civilian use. This extremely serious behavior is enough to prove that the German government has intentionally or unintentionally made negotiations impossible, as the foundation of the negotiations has been completely destroyed by Germany's actions.

Therefore, before discussing whether an agreement can be reached on a way to implement guarantees that would allow the countries signing the treaty to recognize Germany's rearmament as legitimate, France must put its concerns about its own security conditions first. The text continues that Germany's return to the League of Nations would actually alleviate this worry, ending by saying that Germany's return to Geneva has been seen as a necessary condition to achieve a satisfactory way to implement guarantees. Eden's trip to Germany did not bring back a good solution on this important point, and hopes today do not seem much better than before. (Reuters dispatch, 18th)

France's Attitude Is Firm in Opposing German Rearmament 37

(Paris) France's attitude towards the disarmament issue has been consistent. This is the conclusion we have reached after reading France's reply to the UK. France also believes that Germany's reasons for wanting to spend 2 billion marks on military expenses are insufficient. Therefore, the French government believes that Germany's increase in armaments is a secret operation and refuses to formally recognize it. When Germany is determined to rearm, France can only bring the discussion on the disarmament issue back to a proper plan, in other words, to discuss disarmament within the scope of the disarmament conference and the League of Nations. Therefore, Germany's return to Geneva is of great significance, because whether the German authorities have good intentions and are sincere will be determined by whether Germany returns to Geneva. The French official document will inevitably cause a reaction in the UK, but the general public hopes that British public opinion will be able to understand the reasons for France's decision and also feel the need for agreement between Britain and France. As for the German side, after reading the French official document, they should be able to understand that the ambiguous policy has now ended, and that a clear and upright attitude may be the key to success. The French official document will definitely excite the countries of the Little Entente and Poland. In addition, the French government has taken this decision knowing its seriousness and deeply understanding the impact it may have, and believes that this action is for the welfare of the country. (Havas dispatch, 17th)

Comparing French and German Armaments, Who Is Violating the Treaty? Wilhelmstrasse Issues Statement 38

(Berlin) Wilhelmstrasse issued an official statement today, saying that Britain, Italy, and Germany are all pursuing a disarmament policy in a direct and active way. France's claim that Germany has violated the treaty is obviously a tactical move. The treaty contains many possibilities regarding armaments, which Germany has not used. For example, the treaty allows for compensation for scrapped ships, which is one of them. Germany has destroyed its heavy artillery and submarines, but France has more artillery positions and its fleet has increased repeatedly. Who is this directed at? (Reuters dispatch, 19th)

The general public sees the French disarmament note as a clear and firm rejection of the plan proposed by British Prime Minister MacDonald. France now states that it is sincerely opposed to Germany's substantial rearmament, and that it is useless to pretend to negotiate disarmament. Therefore, everyone feels that Eden's suggestion that the main body of the Disarmament Conference should be convened on April 30th is no longer valid. However, the General Committee should meet as soon as possible. It is also believed that Germany's reaction to the French note will inevitably be severe, because one of the major powers has now spoken clearly for the first time, placing the responsibility for the current situation on Germany's shoulders. American Financial Deficit 48

(Washington) The American fiscal year ends on June 30th. As of the 16th of this month, the total national treasury deficit reached 3,072,988,066 yuan, which is even greater than the total deficit for the entire year of 1933. (Havas dispatch, 18th)

Indo-Japanese Agreement Established 49

(Tokyo) Foreign Minister Hirota telegraphed Japanese envoy to India, Sawada, today to sign the first word of the Japan-India cotton industry agreement. The agreement is for a period of three years. Japan can import 125 million yards of cotton cloth into India without the obligation to purchase Indian cotton. However, Japan must purchase 10 million bales of Indian cotton as an exchange for importing 225 million yards of cotton cloth into India. The maximum amount of cotton cloth imported into India is 400 million yards. Any cotton purchased in excess in any year will be included in the account for the following year. Cotton cloth is divided into four categories, with grey cloth accounting for the largest amount, accounting for 45 percent. The next is colored cloth, accounting for 34 percent. A tax of 50 percent will be levied on all imported cotton cloth, according to the current tax rate of 75 percent. The agreement grants Japan the most-favored-nation treatment. (Reuters dispatch, 19th)

The United States Prepares to Commemorate Lafayette's Centennial Anniversary 52

(Washington) In 1783, French General Lafayette, under the orders of King Louis XVI of France, crossed the ocean to America to assist Washington in fighting the British army. Lafayette contributed to American independence. Lafayette died in France on May 20, 1834, and Americans held a grand memorial ceremony for him. This year marks the centennial anniversary of Lafayette's death. Congress has decided to hold a commemoration on May 20th, which will follow the ceremony adopted a century ago. President Roosevelt will deliver a speech as President Jackson did a century ago. French Ambassador to the United States, Trabut, will also be invited to participate on that day. Congress has now formed a committee to prepare for the commemoration ceremony. Congressman Byrns recently presented the resolution passed by Congress in 1834 to President Roosevelt for review. This case ordered members of Congress to mourn Lafayette, and both Congress and the outside world wore black gauze for 30 days. (Havas dispatch, 18th)

(London) Imperial Chemical Industries of the United Kingdom has recently researched the use of the "hydrogenation method" to extract kerosene from coal. This method has been tested for a long time and has been effective, but it has not yet been industrialized. Li Yuankai Talks About the Yunnan-Burma Border Dispute 55

(Nanjing) Chiang Kai-shek telegraphed Li Yuankai to go to Jiangxi for consultation on the Ban Hong incident. Li has returned to Nanjing. According to him, (1) when the incident occurred, most of the information was not accurate. His hometown is very close to Ban Hong, so he knows more details than outsiders. Ban Hong and Ban Nong are only 80 li apart. When the border was demarcated in the 27th year of Guangxu, five major lines were originally set, namely the so-called red, purple, and other lines. Among them, three major lines were demarcated at that time. The remaining two lines were one in the southern section, where Yunnan Province borders Annam, and one in the northern section, where Burma borders the Sichuan-Tibet area. (2) Yunnan Province has the most complex ethnic groups. The largest ethnic group is the Kata ethnic group, followed by the Hui ethnic group living in concentrated areas. Ban Nong is the Kata ethnic group, and Ban Hong is a local person from Yunnan Province. This incident was a conflict between the Ban Nong ethnic group and the Ban Hong local people. British troops were stationed, but not in Ban Nong, and whether the people of Ban Nong were instructed by the British to forcibly mine silver mines is not easy to determine. (3) The silver mine in Ban Hong Pianma, which is thousands of li long, is the best in the world. There are also many gold mines, followed by coal, iron, and other mines everywhere, and silver mines are the best. Most of the local people still mine by indigenous methods and do not know how to refine them, so the silver mined contains many impurities. If the mined silver is refined with machine furnaces, the composition will naturally increase. The silver mine in that area has indeed attracted the attention of foreigners. He was previously ordered by Chiang Kai-shek to go to Jiangxi to report in detail. Chiang Kai-shek ordered that when going to survey the border, the original central plan should still be carried out. After returning to Nanjing, he has repeatedly consulted with the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. The commissioners who will go to survey the border together are still being selected and will be selected soon. (5) The survey of the border is expensive, and the central government has not yet decided. Once it is received, they will set off. This time, they will only survey the border of Yunnan Province, including Ban Hong and other places, according to the original line, and then report to the central government for approval. As for sending personnel to measure and demarcate the border, it will be necessary for the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to inform the British consul in Kunming and the British diplomatic commissioner in Rangoon, and then ask the government of that country for instructions before both parties can schedule a joint survey. (Special telegram, 19th)

(Guangzhou) It is reported that the chairman of Yunnan has now sent the director of the Department of Education to Guangdong to explain the Yunnan border dispute. The official has arrived in the territory of Guangxi and will arrive in Guangdong Province in a few days. The chairman of Yunnan is now urging that the border between Yunnan Province and Burma be demarcated as soon as possible to avoid future disputes. This negotiation is currently underway. (Reuters dispatch, 19th)

Situation of Public Bonds Issued Since the Founding of the Republic of China 60

(Nanjing) According to the Public Debt Department of the Ministry of Finance, since the founding of the Republic of China, 58 types of national treasury securities of various natures have been issued domestically. 28 types were issued by the Beijing government, 1 type was issued by the Wuhan government, and 9 types were issued by the Nanjing National Government, totaling 1,761,152,782 yuan. As of the end of the 20th year of the Republic of China, after repaying and recovering 843,404,829 yuan annually, there are 38 types of outstanding bonds, with a total principal amount of 917,748,152 yuan. There are also 70 types of unsecured domestic debt and other national treasury securities, with a principal amount of 40,542,181 yuan. In addition, the Guangdong government issued the first, second, and third prize-bearing public bonds. Excluding the principal and canceled tickets, the actual debt is 19,086,775 Haikwan taels, which is converted to 15,269,420 yuan in national currency at an 80% discount. The Hankou Treasury bills are valued at 8,599,053 yuan. The above three items are not included. If calculated together, the total amount of outstanding debt is 982,158,807 yuan (19th Special Dispatch).

In addition, Zhang Kaiyun and Huang Shaowen, two comrades from the Tianjin Municipal Party Department, were successively murdered by rioters. It was decided that Huang Shaowen would be given 1,000 yuan for funeral expenses and Zhang Kaiyun would be given 500 yuan for funeral expenses. Additional compensation will also be requested (19th Central News Agency Dispatch).

(Nanjing) According to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, the British Legation has informed that Australian Deputy Prime Minister and Minister of Foreign Affairs Latham, accompanied by his wife and ten staff members, will come to China by mail ship to investigate the politics and economy of various countries. Control Yuan Requests Disciplinary Action Against Gu Renfa; Yang Rentian Files an Impeachment Case 64

(Nanjing) Control Yuan member Yang Rentian filed an impeachment case against Gu Renfa for dereliction of duty, stating that he recently read in the newspaper that Liu Zhuomin, the director of the Second Public Security Branch in Wuxi, Jiangsu, refused to be transferred and was shielded by Li Shuyun, the wife of the Director of the Civil Affairs Department, Gu Renfa. Since Liu was so ignorant and incompetent, Gu Renfa, the director of the department, personally appointed him. His failure to investigate personnel carefully constitutes dereliction of duty. According to the director of the department, Li Shuyun and her mother also engaged in various illegal activities such as soliciting and accepting bribes, and eight types of evidence were presented. However, he did not report it until after the Liu case occurred, which shows his negligence of duty. Regardless of the content of the case reported in various newspapers, which is bizarre, the director of the department is responsible for his dereliction of duty on these two points alone. It is requested that Director Gu Renfa be transferred for disciplinary action to maintain official integrity. After being reviewed by Control Yuan members Wang Zizhuang and others, it was believed that Gu Renfa's improper use of personnel and negligence of duty were obvious facts and commonly known by the public. He should be punished according to law. The original case documents have been submitted by the Control Yuan to Chairman Lin of the National Government for review and implementation (19th Special Dispatch).

Ministry of Industry Advocates Reorganizing the Kailuan Mining Bureau with Equal Rights for Chinese and British Parties 65

(Nanjing) According to the Ministry of Industry, the Kailuan Mining Bureau was formed by the merger of the Kaiping and Luanzhou mines and has been in operation for more than 20 years. Due to capital relations, the power is in the hands of the British, and the general manager must be appointed by the British, while the Chinese side is the deputy. The supervisors sent by the ministry in the past could not interfere in mining affairs and only received salaries without doing any work. The business profits are also limited by the contract. Within profits of 3 million yuan, the profits are divided 60% to the British and 40% to the Chinese. During the recent mining crisis, General Manager Norson and Deputy Manager Gu Zhenlai came to the Ministry of Industry in Beijing to report on the situation. The Ministry of Industry advocated reorganization, establishing a new contract with equal rights for the Chinese and British parties, and dividing the annual profits equally. Norson and Gu have returned to Tianjin to start preparations. It is still undecided when it will be implemented (19th Special Dispatch).

Soviet Civil Aviation (Moscow Dispatch via Reuters) 106

Recently in the Soviet capital, there was a very unusual celebration. A group of Soviet aviators congratulated one of their colleagues whose total flight distance had been enough to circle the Earth twenty-five times. This navigator had flown over one million kilometers (kilometers), carrying mail and cargo without experiencing a single serious accident. There are ten such aviators in the Soviet Union, but their fame is known only to a very few. Only those who break records by flying thousands of kilometers immediately gain fame at home and abroad, while those who fly hundreds of thousands of kilometers in daily work are unknown to anyone.

However, this kind of daily work is filled with the essence of true chivalric novels. For example, there was one aviator who flew a light aircraft in forty-degree below-zero weather to several northern trading posts to deliver furs needed by the international fur market on time. Hundreds of navigators fly every day, either to rescue steamships surrounded by ice, or to transport goods to residents in the high mountains of Central Asia, or to patrol forests, or to deliver mail, or to eliminate locusts and mosquitoes, or to sow rice, wheat and hay, or to spread smoke over fields to protect them from frost, or to put out forest fires, etc. This has indeed greatly contributed to the Soviet aviation industry.

The Birth of the Soviet Aviation Industry 107

But before such vigorous development, Soviet aviation had gone through a considerable stage. The first air route (from Moscow to Berlin, a total of 1,500 kilometers) was established in 1923. In the past decade, the progress of Soviet civil aviation has been rapid, like a thousand miles a day. In terms of route length, it now ranks third in the world (after the United States and France), but in terms of several special types of aviation, it already ranks first. At the beginning of the first five-year plan, the total length of aviation routes was 9,326 kilometers. During this five-year period, the routes increased two and a half times, reaching 32,000 kilometers. This year, the route length has been increased by another 12,000 kilometers. In addition, the Soviet Union has more than 10,000 kilometers of circular postal routes. Ukraine, the North Caucasus, Western Siberia, Central Asia, and other regions of the Soviet Union are covered with routes to transport mail and provide guidance for agricultural operations, etc. This year, the length of these circular routes is expected to increase to about 25,000 kilometers.

One of the World's Longest Air Routes 108

Several of the current Soviet air routes, such as the Moscow-Vladivostok line and the Moscow-Tbilisi-Tashkent line, are among the longest in the world. Aviation plays a very important role in transporting urgent mail, goods, and passengers on important missions. In 1932, aviation transported 38,000 passengers, 700 tons of mail, and 2,000 tons of goods. Last year, these numbers increased greatly. Passengers increased to 55,000, freight transport increased by 170 percent, and mail transport increased by 385 percent. This year, Soviet shipping operations should increase at least double compared to last year.

Flying Over Deserts and Ice 109

Aviation is most useful in sparsely populated and barren areas. In the desert and mountainous regions of Central Asia, and in the Arctic zone, aviation has achieved a landmark revolution. In some places in Central Asia, residents are completely unaware of what cars and automobiles are, but they know airplanes very well. In the past, it took months to travel from cities such as Tashkent or Samarkand to remote rural areas of Central Asia. Now, Soviet aircraft have connected these remote residents with central cities in one or two days.

Aviation is of great significance to the Arctic zone. Soviet aviators have also established regular relations with remote trading posts there. Soviet islands in the Arctic Ocean are visited by airplanes every year. Last year, Soviet aircraft flew as far as Wrangel Island six times.

The aircraft serving the Karsk expedition saves the country millions of dollars every year, because the aircraft can point out areas of "clear water" to the ships and guide them through the ice.

Dirigible Manufacturing Takes Off 110

The Soviet Union started manufacturing airships not long ago, but it has already built several small airships (the largest with a capacity of 7,500 cubic meters). These small airships are just experimental models, a prelude to the future manufacturing of large airships. At the same time, the Soviet Union is also manufacturing training boats to train navigators.

The Soviet Union's first medium-sized airship is nearing completion, and construction has begun on another experimental all-metal airship. During the second five-year plan, the engineering will be expanded to build a small squadron of airships. This squadron (to be named the "Lenin Squadron") will consist of seven large airships. Now the Soviet people are raising donations of 25 million rubles for the construction of this fleet of airships, and plans are being made to establish several airship routes to connect the central cities of the Soviet Union with the Arctic zone. The Effectiveness of Aviation in Agriculture

Soviet agricultural aviation ranks first in the world in terms of its work volume. This is not surprising, because the conditions for the development of agricultural aviation can only arise in the Soviet Union. In 1931, agricultural aviation began experiments with aerial sowing. In that year, only 4,000 hectares were sown. Two years later, this number had increased to 138,000 hectares. An aircraft can sow 20 hectares per hour, which is nine times the output of a tractor. In addition to sowing, Soviet agricultural aviation also performs a great deal of work in eliminating pests. Last year, aviation services were used on 415,000 hectares of land. In low-lying areas, aircraft can spray naphtha to eliminate mosquitoes and can drop other materials to eliminate other pests.

Agricultural aviation also has many other functions. For example, in winter, when dense frost is prevalent, only aircraft can create impermeable smoke screens. Aircraft can also patrol forests, prevent fires, take films of forest areas, eliminate weeds, etc.

Soviet Civil Aviation is First in the World 111

In terms of aerial photography, Soviet civil aviation is already first in the world. Last year, films were taken from the sky of the Kamchatka Peninsula and the Lena River Delta. Civil aviation on this scale would not have been possible in such a short period of time without a domestic aviation industry. The Soviet scientific aviation organization has made great achievements in careful planning. All Soviet air routes now use domestically produced aircraft, but three or four years ago, most of the aircraft were manufactured abroad. The quality of Soviet aircraft is now no less than that of foreign aircraft, and some models are even better than those abroad. The Soviet Union is a pioneer in the manufacture of all-metal aircraft and holds the leading position in the world.

The manufacture of aircraft engines is the most important part of the aircraft manufacturing industry. In this regard, the Soviet Union has also achieved great success. In 1930, only 12 percent of aircraft used Soviet engines. Now, the words "Made in the Soviet Union" are engraved on 90 percent of aviation engines. (The End)

Military Situation in the Far East (Vladivostok Dispatch) Preparation for Defensive Posture, Response to Sudden Changes 112

The ominous dark clouds over the Pacific seem to have temporarily dissipated, but in a corner of the Far East, from the upper reaches of the Heilongjiang River to the Tongjiang estuary, along the Ussuri River, a gloomy atmosphere prevails. Everyone has a sense that major and concerning events will occur in the near future. In particular, the movement of Japanese troops this time has further stimulated the nerves of the Soviet authorities. According to the information obtained here, the replacement of two divisions of the Japanese army is by no means a simple troop rotation. It has two very serious implications: first, to take advantage of the situation to attack Siberia and expand its power; and second, to find an opportunity to invade Inner Mongolia, extend its reach to Xinjiang, and implement the second step of its continental policy. Therefore, the replacement troops sent to Manchuria this time are the two largest divisions, Kyoto and Nagoya. Because the transportation in northern Manchuria has not been fully developed, the Himeji 10th Division, which excels in infantry and artillery, can only cope with volunteers lacking military equipment. To engage in international battles and compete with the Red Army, it is not enough. The Nagoya Division is equipped with a full tank regiment and more than 200 aircraft. These troops are concentrated in Heilongjiang, Harbin, Hailin and other places. Although they are not fully deployed, they are very active.

The Soviet Union, which aims to maintain its national territory and build a socialist country, will certainly not ignore such military actions, nor will it casually relax its own military defense work. In the general state of the Soviet Union, ordinary people have no way of knowing the military situation, and foreigners are absolutely not allowed to know. However, based solely on what I can see and what is generally known, I will give a brief report. It is only clear to senior Soviet generals responsible for the situation how many troops are stationed along the Manchurian border and what types of units they are. Our estimates and general observations are that there are no more than 200,000 troops at most, and at least 140,000. The types of troops included are very complex, including assault infantry, crack cavalry, huge air force, with at least 300 aircraft, as well as chemical warfare teams and mechanized corps. A flight field near Vladivostok is particularly large and accommodates a particularly large number of aircraft. The aircraft also have a strong range and can certainly make round trips to Changchun and Fengtian without any problems. Even round trips to Tokyo and Osaka are not difficult.

The port of Vladivostok is more of a commercial port than a military port. In fact, it does not have any particularly remarkable facilities. In the reporter's view, it is not easy to resist the superior Japanese navy. However, they pay great attention to coastal defense. They are currently building strong fortresses. At the same time, twelve submarines are stationed on Russky Island. In fact, it is feared that the air force and the army will ultimately protect Vladivostok.

Judging from this situation, the war between the Soviet Union and Japan is truly on the verge of breaking out. Moreover, the two countries are historical enemies. The emotions of the general public and the current political system are very discordant. The final moment is always inevitable. Therefore, they are all engaged in active defense work and are deploying troops.

However, the current problem is that the Soviet Union will never cross the border to challenge, let alone turn to military offensive, so as to cause huge disadvantages to its own construction. If the Japanese Empire suddenly goes crazy and attacks Siberia or the coastal provinces, it will provoke a catastrophe. However, Japan not only contains irreconcilable contradictions in ordinary society, but also has many dangerous elements in its army, where they are fermenting. In particular, the army stationed in northern Manchuria is more susceptible to red influence. Furthermore, the anti-Japanese movement in Manchuria, although superficially latent, is even more solid and powerful in secret, making the Japanese Empire uneasy. Therefore, recently, it has shown signs of easing. The only symbol of this is its expression of acceptance of the Soviet Union's proposal on the China Eastern Railway issue. A meeting will be reopened soon to discuss the price and other issues. Although the future of the meeting may not be immediately optimistic, the pressure of the situation cannot but make Japan retreat slightly. However, this is only a temporary phenomenon after all, and the elements of war still exist. (April 10, 1934)

Three-Route Army Recovers Ganzhu City Bandits Retreat Towards Guangchang and Ningdu 113

Nanchang Dispatch: Recently, the Third Route Army, advancing from Nanfeng, Lichuan, and southward, successively captured Baishe and Jigongshan, located on the border between Nanfeng and Guangchang, and then advanced towards Guangchang. On the morning of the 13th, Fu Zhongfang's division, after departing from Baishe Town, passed through Ziling Mountain south of Luofang and attacked the bandits in the rain. At noon, Li's regiment captured the defenses of the bandit army's 55th and 71st units. Shortly after, Zhu's regiment captured areas around Liujiabao and Jiangjundu. At that time, a part of the pseudo-Ninth Army Corps and the pseudo-Fourteenth Division, guarding the blockhouses, stubbornly resisted with their defenses. After a fierce battle lasting half a day, more than a dozen bandit blockhouses were destroyed by the late afternoon, and many bandits were killed. The remnants of the bandits retreated in droves towards the mountains on the border between Ningdu and Guangchang in the southwest. The Third Route Army then recovered Ganzhu City. The headquarters recently announced Chen Cheng's victory telegram, stating that in the battle to capture Ganzhu, more than 200 bandits were killed, dozens of bandits were captured, six or seven heavy machine guns and more than 200 rifles were seized. The advance towards the south is still in progress. Ganzhu is a vital pass in the northern part of Guangchang, only a few dozen miles away from Guangchang City. Once the East Route Army arrives in Jianning, which borders Guangchang, the armies of Yongfeng, Le'an, Yihuang, and Nanfeng can advance side by side and capture Guangchang and Ningdu. (17th)

Four Provinces Encircle and Suppress Fang's Bandits Zhejiang Security Chief Yu Jishi Arrives in Jiangxi 21st Division Captures Xiangu Mountain in Shangrao 114

Nanchang Dispatch: Fang Zhimin's Red Bandits, with Hengfeng as their base, have been entrenched in the border areas of Jiangxi, Anhui, Zhejiang, and Fujian for seven years, with Rao and Xin counties suffering the most. Chairman Chiang Kai-shek specially ordered the armies of four provinces to encircle and suppress them. Chen Tiaoyuan's troops moved from the Anhui border from north to south, and Yu Jishi's troops from Zhejiang Security moved from east to west, together with Liang Lizhu's troops, originally in Guangfeng, Shangrao, and Qianshan, and the garrison troops in Yujiang and Wannian, to form a four-sided encirclement. In addition to Commander-in-Chief Chen's arrival in Wuyuan, Zhejiang Security Chief Yu Jishi, accompanied by more than a dozen staff members, arrived in Yushan by Hangjiang Road train at 10 a.m. on the 7th. Acting Commander Chiang Wang County Chief and all circles welcomed them at the station, stationed at the headquarters, and inquired in detail about the local situation of bandit suppression and post-war affairs. On the 11th, all circles in Yushan held a joint celebration to express their welcome. All the security teams entering Jiangxi from Zhejiang have also completely arrived at their destinations, and the newly transferred and joined reinforcements have also been deployed. Chen Tiaoyuan, Zhao Guantao, Liang Lizhu, Tang Huiyuan, and others are all commanding in various places, adopting an encirclement and blockade policy against the bandits. The 21st Division in Shangrao recently captured the bandit lair of Xiangu Mountain in Shangrao. The division sent a telegram to the headquarters reporting victory, saying: "Xiangu Mountain is surrounded by cliffs on all sides, with only a small path in the northwest for people to climb. The bandits have built blockhouses there, and there are obstacles such as deer fences, which are extremely strong. The Shangrao Pseudo-Independent Battalion occupies the blockhouse, and the rest are on guard around the perimeter. Our 21st Division sent a team to suppress them, first defeating their guard team, and then encircling Xiangu Mountain. They launched a bloody charge along the small path, and after a fierce battle of six hours, they finally seized the mountain. In this battle, a total of 54 bandits were captured, and three bandits, including company commander Zheng Chongyang and platoon leader Cai Dongzhi, and more than 90 soldiers were killed. Thirty-one rifles, two carbines, two pistols, one submachine gun, and one air-pressure gun were seized." (17th)

Sichuan Bandits Launch Large-Scale Counteroffensive Fierce Frontal Battle Bandit Losses Heavy Tang's Troops Victorious, Now Confront Bandits Across River Chiang Kai-shek Praises Third and Fifth Route Armies in Telegram to Liu Xiang 115

Hankou Dispatch: Xu Xiangqian's remnant bandits, having failed in Nanba, retreated to Tongjiang. They were already at the end of their rope, but because the occupied area was shrinking and the defense line was shortened, the troop strength was concentrated. The bandits knew that the gain or loss of Tongjiang was a matter of survival, so they decided to stake everything on a single throw and launch a fierce counteroffensive. Liu Xiang's direct Fifth Route Army was their sole target, as this route had the thickest troop strength and sufficient arms and ammunition. The front was mostly high mountains and ridges, where bandits could occupy high ground and have the advantage. If this route were broken, the other routes would be easily swept away. On the 14th, the Fifth Route Army began to advance fiercely towards Luodingzhai, Niupanzhai, Qianqiu'e, Dashanbei, Mashikou, Jinlongtai, Datikou, Xin Genliang, and other places. The bandits also launched a large-scale counteroffensive at this time. Officers and soldiers fought fiercely with bandits, engaging in hand-to-hand combat on cliffs and precipices, charging back and forth, gaining and losing ground at times. After a day and night of fierce fighting, the officers and soldiers gained an advantage with the help of aircraft and artillery, but the bandit counteroffensive continued as before. Xu himself was stationed in Tongjiang and specially appointed the pseudo-military division commanders as supervisors, personally commanding on the front line. Those responsible for charging were selected cadres from Hunan and Hubei, all experienced and exceptionally brave. On the 16th, the bandit momentum weakened slightly, and they retreated across the Sita River to hold their positions. The officers and soldiers approached the river, but due to the fatigue of the soldiers, they did not launch a strong crossing and temporarily formed a stalemate. In this bloody battle lasting three days, both sides suffered heavy losses. Tang Shizun, commander-in-chief of the Fifth Route Army, telegraphed the general headquarters in Xuanhan on the 16th, reporting the details of the battle, stating that "The bandits facing us yesterday took advantage of our offensive to concentrate the majority of their forces and their main force, and stubbornly resisted and launched repeated counteroffensives, intending to seek another way out. When our various units attacked Luodingzhai, Niupanzhai, Qianqiu'e, Da'ekou, and Xin Genliang and reached the mountainside, the bandits launched a fierce assault, attempting to force us to fall off the cliffs. Fortunately, our officers and soldiers fought bravely, repeatedly engaging in hand-to-hand combat, with blood and flesh flying everywhere. After a day of hard fighting, and with the concentrated bombardment of machine guns and artillery, and the assistance of the air force, we finally recovered the various positions and occupied them firmly. At night, we ordered the various units to select elite troops and launch a night attack. Although the cliffs of Changyan'e, Jinlongtai, and Luoding Niupan were steep, and the ravines were several zhang deep, the officers and soldiers did not avoid the difficulties and finally occupied Mashikou, Fuxingchang, and Guanzi Ling at 3 a.m. At dawn, we pursued to the line of Changtan River, Yankou River, Kuzhutan, and Shuangtanzi, and completely cleared the south bank of the Xiaobei River. Currently, the bandits are confronting us along the line of Sitan River, Changtan River, Yankou River, Wangshui River, and Taijia River. In this battle, hundreds of bandits were captured, more than 200 rifles and more than ten White-Kerman machine guns were seized, and twenty or thirty supervisory officer and unit flags were captured. The bodies of bandits killed were scattered across the fields, and after examining the symbols, there were more than one hundred regimental, battalion, and company commanders and supervisory officers. The intensity of this battle was unprecedented in the various bandit suppression campaigns of this route. We are still continuing to cross the river and attack strongly. Tang Shizun bowed respectfully." Also, Liu Xiang telegraphed that on the 14th and 15th, in the battles of Luodingzhai and others, the bandits launched ten-odd assaults with cadres engaging in hand-to-hand combat, and the officers and soldiers suffered thousands of casualties, and the bandits were about twice as many. According to aerial reports, the bandits are still sending large reinforcements, continuously, intending to have a final decisive battle with the Fifth Route Army. There will be even more fierce battles in the next two days. Li Qixiang, commander-in-chief of the Third Route Army, and Tian Songyao, commander-in-chief of the Second Route Army, also telegraphed victories. Li's telegram stated, "At dawn the day before yesterday, hundreds of bandits attacked, and after our Li Zongfang's brigade bravely engaged them, the bandits collapsed and retreated to Longbeizhai. At the same time, Li Qingting's brigade also attacked the bandits in Jianshanping. After a fierce battle until noon, they broke through two lines of bandit fortifications, seizing a banner of the first battalion of the pseudo-270th regiment, thirty rifles, and capturing dozens of bandits. On the evening of the next day, the bandits attacked Li Qingting's brigade's position from Huangniba. We waited for them to penetrate deep, and ambushed them from three sides, inflicting heavy losses on the bandits, and they fled in disarray. This morning, upon inspection, there were corpses lying all over the ground, about fifty or more. This morning, Li Qingting's brigade continued to attack Jianshanping, but the bandits still stubbornly resisted. It was not until noon that the bandit position was broken through, capturing sixty or seventy bandits and seizing more than forty rifles. At the same time, Li Zongfang's brigade attacked Longchengzhai and is still fighting in Nanhua." Tian's telegram stated, "Our left column fought fiercely with the bandits in Yinlingshan, killing more than 300 bandits and seizing more than 100 rifles, and then occupied Zhenziba. The remaining 5,000-odd bandits all retreated to the left bank, and we dispatched Hu Yisheng's brigade, Zhao and Zhang's two regiments, and Luo Naiqiong's division's Xue brigade to join forces and encircle and suppress them, pursuing them to Rentoushan, killing countless bandits. The remaining bandits fled to Heishuitan and Lingshanchang, and are being pursued." Chairman Chiang, in view of the valiant fighting of the Third and Fifth Route Armies, sent a special telegram to Liu Xiang praising them, stating, "Your Third and Fifth Routes have made progress and have captured many prisoners. The officers and soldiers are fighting valiantly, which is commendable. We hope that you will instruct your subordinates to be even more diligent. Chiang Kai-shek bowed." (18th)

Ministry of Industry Bans Accountants from Holding Concurrent Positions 116

It is clearly stipulated in the Accountant Regulations that accountants shall not hold other positions or engage in industrial and commercial businesses, but it has been found that there are many accountants in various places who violate this provision and perform their duties illegally. In order to enforce laws and regulations, the Ministry of Industry has instructed the government agencies in charge of accountants to take action in accordance with the law. The notification letter from the Nanjing Municipal Social Bureau to various accountants is copied below: According to the Ministry of Industry's Instruction No. Shang Zi 25132, "It has been found that accountants, after registration, shall not hold other positions or engage in industrial and commercial businesses in addition to those listed in Article 1 of the Accountant Regulations. Articles 11 and 12 of the Accountant Regulations have clearly stipulated this, and the matters in which they may not perform their duties in the name of an accountant have also been stipulated in Article 13 of the same regulations. All accountants should abide by these regulations. However, the number of those who have obtained the qualifications of an accountant is increasing, and the number of those who have applied for registration to practice is also large. It is inevitable that there will be violations of the regulations among them. In order to enforce laws and regulations, it is appropriate to order your department to immediately and thoroughly investigate the above-mentioned legal provisions. Once it is found that there are situations such as holding concurrent positions or engaging in industrial and commercial businesses, action should be taken in accordance with the law. You are required to comply with this order and report the handling situation at any time. This order," etc. In accordance with this order, you are hereby notified to comply with this order. If there are concurrent positions or engagement in industrial and commercial businesses, you should immediately decide whether to abandon or report to suspend the performance of your duties in accordance with the provisions of Article 9 of the Accountant Regulations. If you conceal and fail to report, or illegally perform your duties, you will be dealt with once discovered in order to uphold the rule of law. This is hereby notified.

Record of the Commencement Ceremony for Dredging the River in Songjiang The City River in the Urban Area has been Silted for a Long Time and Needs Dredging After 117

Magistrate Jin Tigan and local gentry jointly prepared and planned for three months, and the preparations have been completed. The surveyed length of the main and tributary rivers to be dredged reaches more than 36 li, and the cost is estimated to be about 60,000 yuan. The government provides a subsidy of 28,000 yuan, and the remaining funds are raised locally, with donations divided into two types: A, a special donation, and B, two months of rent, with landlords and tenants each bearing half. Donations are levied based on the estimated value of residences. The construction department of Shanghai Taichang Gravel Company is contracted to carry out the work, and the approval of the Construction Department has been obtained. The dredging process will start from the first and sixth sections. After one section is dredged, another section will be dredged in order to maintain the people's drinking water supply. A dam has now been built at Huayang Bridge to pump water. This river project is the first major project in Songjiang. Therefore, the commencement ceremony was held at 2 p.m. today (19th) at Dongchan Temple. Magistrate Jin, together with all the members of the River Dredging Committee and the directors of each section, attended the meeting. Representatives from the County Party Headquarters, various agencies, and newspaper reporters also attended. Magistrate Jin presided over the meeting and performed the ceremony as usual. Secretary Wu Zhongyu and Party Headquarters Representative Shen Yuxuan gave speeches. Magistrate Jin then addressed the river workers, who were all from other places, especially gathering the foremen, saying that all river workers should wear symbols, and the location of the mud piles had been specified. If anyone took the opportunity to extort or demand things, they would be severely punished without mercy. The meeting was adjourned after the ceremony.

County Government Convenes and Instructs Book Writers 118

The county government, in accordance with provincial government orders, has mandated that all people's national tax payments from this year onwards will be accompanied by the immediate issuance of a string of receipts. This will both simplify procedures and prevent corruption. In the past, before collecting taxes, the book writers would first create a register of grain-producing households, based on which the string of receipts would be prepared. Now, as the old system is being changed, the Chief of the Vehicle Section convened all eighty-four book writers to the government office on this day to give instructions, ordering them to create the register as soon as possible to meet the need for issuing receipts at any time.

Suzhou Defense Corps undergoes Another Reorganization 119

The defense corps in various districts of Wu County, both urban and rural, has been ordered to reorganize. It is planned to establish three independent detachments in the urban area and twenty branches in the rural area. Recently, the autonomous regions of Wu County were also ordered to change, with the original twenty-three urban and rural districts being merged into thirteen rural districts and two urban districts. Therefore, the urban and rural defense corps should also be reorganized. It is proposed to establish one squadron in the urban area and six independent platoons in the rural area. This plan has been submitted to the provincial government for approval by the county government.

Gu Xin Went to Nanjing Last Night and then to Jiangxi - Requesting Instructions on the Share Funds of the Grain Transportation and Sales Bureau and the Uniform Collection of Foreign Rice Tax 134

The matter of organizing the Grain Transportation and Sales Bureau of eight provinces and cities has been in preparation for several months, but it has been difficult to establish because the share funds from various parties have not been remitted in full. The transportation and sale of grain is related to the regulation of domestic grain, so the establishment of the bureau is urgent. Gu Xin, the chairman of the preparatory office of the bureau, accompanied Zhou Minggang, the director of the Grain Section of the Fourth Department of the Municipal Social Bureau, on the overnight express train to Nanjing yesterday afternoon at 11:00, and will then go to Nanchang to meet with Chairman Chiang Kai-shek to report on the progress of preparations and request instructions on remedial measures. According to the Central News Agency reporter, Zhou, the director of the Municipal Social Bureau, said that in addition to requesting Chairman Chiang Kai-shek to order all provinces and cities to remit the share funds of the Grain Transportation and Sales Bureau in full as soon as possible, he will also request Chairman Chiang Kai-shek to order all provinces and cities to strictly comply with the unified collection of the foreign rice tax and will also visit the competent authorities in the capital to seek solutions in order to achieve this goal as soon as possible. The memorandum Gu presented to Chairman Chiang Kai-shek is recorded as follows: "I believe that to save the rural crisis, the first priority is to prevent the dumping of foreign rice, and to prevent the dumping of foreign rice, it is necessary to unify the tax rates in Guangdong and Fujian. Therefore, the association has repeatedly appealed and telegraphed the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Finance, and Your Excellency, requesting that the provinces of Guangdong and Fujian be ordered to immediately impose taxes in accordance with the current import tax rate on foreign rice. On the 10th of this month, I received a telegram from Your Excellency replying that it had been forwarded to the Ministry of Finance for verification. It has been half a month since then, and the people of the country have been looking forward to it, but the Ministry of Finance has not made any indication. However, I have seen in the newspaper that the Ministry of Finance replied to the Wuhu Chamber of Commerce that the Guangdong Provincial Government must first agree to abolish the foreign rice tax before the customs can collect the import tax. In this situation, I do not know how long it will be delayed, and after the Fujian Province increased the tax last month, it was only one-half of the customs duty, and there has been no news of any further increase to this day. The leakage in South China has given the powers the opportunity to economically invade and dump foreign rice, causing the rice-producing provinces to hoard grain and seal it, prices to fall, the people to be exhausted, and the rural economy to be in a state of desperation. The people are in a panic and have no peace. The common people are mired in deep water and fire, saving the people from their troubles with a single hand, and ultimately putting hundreds of millions of living beings in water and fire. The government and orders of Fujian Province have long been unified, and it is easy to levy taxes in accordance with the precedents. Although the Guangdong foreign rice tax is related to the provincial treasury, the method proposed by the association can be adopted, incorporated into the customs collection, and the original tax amount can still be returned by the customs for the time being, which is not difficult to implement. The association is deeply disturbed by the urgency of the situation and urges Your Excellency to review the matter and order the Ministry of Finance to immediately increase taxes in accordance with the current import tax rate on foreign rice in the provinces of Fujian and Guangdong. I am eagerly awaiting your orders. Respectfully presented by Gu Xin, Chairman of the Shanghai Grains Industry Association and the Bean and Rice Industry Association, to Chiang Kai-shek, Chairman of the National Government Military Council."

Representatives of the Silk and Satin and Electrical Machinery Industries Went to Nanjing Yesterday to Petition - Regarding the Guangzhou Zhongxing Company's Detention of Domestic Silk 135

The Silk and Satin Industry Association and the Electrical Machinery Silk Weaving Factory Industry Association of this city are indignant at the Guangdong Central Company's detention of domestic silk. After inviting representatives of the Guangbang Silk and Cloth Industry, an emergency joint meeting was specially convened to decide to each send representatives to Beijing and Guangdong with a petition. It is reported that the representatives departed by train yesterday and first went to Beijing to petition. The petitions of the two industry associations and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce are recorded as follows:

The Petition of the Two Industry Associations: "Respectfully presented, the trade associations have repeatedly received letters from members reporting that recently, domestically produced machine-woven silk transported from Shanghai to Guangdong has been identified by the Guangdong Zhongxing Company as foreign goods and required to pay a special tax and detained. The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce has been asked to issue a letter of proof and request its release. After two weeks, the goods have not been returned, and more than 3,000 pieces of goods continue to be detained. As a result, the Guangbang cargo agents have sent telegrams to stop shipping and stop processing, causing terror in the domestic silk business. If we do not fight for it, the day of closing factories and ceasing operations may be imminent. Therefore, at 2 pm on April 17th, a special emergency joint meeting was convened, and representatives of the Guangdong Silk and Cloth Industry Federation were invited to attend to report the detention situation and discuss solutions together. It was unanimously agreed that the Guangdong Zhongxing Company was established specifically to collect special taxes on imported foreign cloth. Its purpose is directly to increase the import tax on foreign goods, with the intention of controlling through taxation. Indirectly, it is to promote domestic goods in order to change the psychology of those who love and use foreign goods. The law is excellent, and the intention is beautiful. However, the company does not do this but instead identifies and detains silk and satin, which are manufactured by domestic factories and meet the national product standards promulgated by the Ministry, without discrimination. This is a strong association and has become an obstacle to the development of domestic silk. It is even contrary to the government's intention to encourage industry and exempt machine-made foreign goods from taxes. At a time when the Ministry of Finance has early measures to abolish miscellaneous taxes and the Southwest Political Affairs Council has decided to have the provincial government order the Finance Department to thoroughly rectify business-run donations and taxes, the company suddenly detains domestic goods and imposes special taxes. I ask whether this special tax is levied on domestic goods. The types of collections compiled by the company can be seen at a glance. What is the crime of silk merchants? Who is willing to bow their heads and obey? If this matter concerns aviation education and talent training, (1) matters concerning how to instill aviation knowledge to the public, (1) matters concerning the establishment of aviation factories and the manufacture of airplanes, (1) matters concerning the aviation industry.

Article 1 of the draft regulations: "The China Aviation Association initiates and convenes the National Aviation Salvation Conference to assist the government in building the aviation industry." Article 2: "This conference is organized by the following representatives: (1) Each provincial and municipal government sends one representative; (2) Each provincial and municipal party department sends one representative; (3) Each provincial and municipal legal entity, such as chambers of commerce, trade unions, agricultural associations, educational associations, and banks or money industries, sends one representative; (4) The Aviation Administration, the Naval Aviation Department, and the Central Aviation School each send one representative; (5) Each provincial aviation agency sends one representative." Article 3: "This conference should be submitted to the Central Party Headquarters, the National Government, and the Military Commission for approval and ask them to send personnel to guide it." Article 4: "This conference establishes a presidium of seven to nine members, who are elected by the attending representatives and take turns chairing the meeting." Article 5: "This conference, in order to facilitate the progress of preparations, is handled by the secretariat organized by the China Aviation Association. When necessary, it may ask related agencies to participate in the preparations. Its organizational rules and detailed rules of procedure will be determined separately." Article 6: "The scope of discussion of this conference is as follows: (1) representative proposals, (2) proposals from provincial and municipal legal entities, (3) party, government, and military proposals, (4) ad hoc proposals." Article 7: "Proposals for this conference must be sent to the China Aviation Association at 132 Rue Lupan, Shanghai, two weeks before the conference's secretariat." Article 8: "The matters decided by this conference will be submitted by the China Aviation Association to the National Government for approval and implementation or sent to the provincial and municipal governments and legal entities for joint implementation." Article 9: "The round-trip travel expenses of the attending representatives of this conference will be borne by the dispatching agency, but the board and lodging expenses during the conference will be covered by the secretariat, and the methods will be determined separately." Article 10: "The venue for this conference is at the YMCA of China at 131 Boulevard des Deux Republiques, Shanghai, and the meeting period is tentatively set from June 15th to June 19th, and may be extended if necessary." Article 11: "The rules of procedure for this conference will be determined separately." Article 12: "These regulations shall be announced and implemented after being approved by the China Aviation Association."

"To the Shanghai Songjiang Fellow-Countrymen Association, for your information. According to the investigation of the dredging costs in the 6th and 14th years of the Republic, neither exceeded 20,000 yuan. This time, according to the county government's announcement, in addition to the 28,000 yuan of construction funds approved by the Provincial Department, there is also a local fundraising portion, requiring a large sum of 35,000 yuan. The two funds combined are more than three times the construction costs during the previous period when rice was expensive. The county government has not publicly announced the detailed budget and contract. Citizens have no way of knowing the secret. Compared with the total construction costs of the previous two river projects, it seems that there is already a surplus. There are no wealthy people in Songjiang society; most are tenants. The fact that they insist on contracting to outsiders indicates collusion for profit, a smoke screen to deceive the citizens. Who will believe it? Songjiang has a surplus of labor but a shortage of wealth. They abandon the surplus and hire outsiders to plunder it. They do not cultivate the shortage but try to squeeze every last drop of fat from it. What is the mindset of those who are supposed to be the parents of the people? Zhuocheng and others have no choice but to petition on behalf of the people. Eurasia Aviation Corporation Adds Direct Route Between Peiping and Canton, Launching May 1st 138

Central News Agency reports that Eurasia Aviation Corporation's planned new routes between Peiping-Shaanxi and Guangdong-Shaanxi are well-equipped and were originally scheduled to launch in January. However, due to the unavailability of the Guangzhou military airfield for borrowing, a separate civil airfield had to be established, causing delays. It is recently heard that the company has negotiated to borrow the Shipai Racecourse as an airfield, and construction is nearing completion, with the launch imminent. Yesterday, a reporter specifically interviewed the General Manager of the company.

Mr. Li Jingcong stated that the company had previously agreed with the Xinjiang authorities that the company's aircraft could resume flights to Dihua by January of this year at the latest, for international through transport, which was expected to be realized at that time. In order to enable direct access to airmail services between Eurasia and Europe between Peiping-Tientsin and Canton-Hong Kong, the company planned to open two new routes between Peiping-Shaanxi and Guangdong-Shaanxi and schedule them to launch at the same time as the resumption of the Xinjiang route in January. This would allow them to intersect with the Shanghai-Xinjiang route in Xi'an, to facilitate the transfer and transport of international airmail between Peiping-Tientsin, Shanghai, Wuhan, Canton, Hong Kong, and other regions with Europe, as well as domestic mail. However, the Xinjiang authorities repeatedly prevented the resumption of flights due to military instability, and problems also arose with the Guangzhou airfield within the Guangdong-Shaanxi route, leading to delays. Now, although the Guangzhou airfield has been relocated and built, the resumption of flights to Xinjiang is difficult to achieve in the short term. The company, considering that the equipment along the Guangdong-Shaanxi and Peiping-Shaanxi routes is already prepared, decided to utilize this equipment to expedite transportation between Peiping and Canton. It was thus decided to change the circuitous flights of Peiping-Shaanxi and Guangdong-Shaanxi to direct flights between Peiping and Canton, to shorten the journey and facilitate travel. This plan has been submitted to the Ministry of Transportation for approval.

The so-called direct Peiping-Canton route involves changing the original Guangdong-Shaanxi route from Guangzhou, via Changsha, Hankou, Xiangyang, to Xi'an, to a route that bypasses Xiangyang and Xi'an, going directly from Hankou to Luoyang. The original Peiping-Shaanxi route from Peiping, via Taiyuan, to Xi'an, is changed to a route that bypasses Taiyuan and Xi'an, going directly from Taiyuan to Luoyang. A through transport route is formed in Luoyang, creating a direct Peiping-Canton route. This not only drastically shortens the journey between Peiping and Canton but also reduces travel time and lowers fares.

Launching on May 1st, although the facilities at each station along the current Peiping-Canton route are already prepared, the company, to ensure all aspects are covered, plans to conduct another inspection of the facilities at each station. It has been decided to send engineer He En by plane this week to inspect the entire route again and has decided to officially open the route on May 1st. The Postal Administration and various stations have been formally notified to send mail and passengers.

Schedule for Southbound and Northbound Flights. The Peiping-Canton route will operate twice a week in each direction. Southbound flights will depart from Peiping every Tuesday and Thursday at 8:00 AM, arriving in Luoyang at 2:00 PM for an overnight stay. They will then depart from Luoyang at 9:00 AM the next morning, arriving in Guangzhou at 6:15 PM on the same day. Northbound flights will depart from Guangzhou every Tuesday and Thursday at 7:00 AM, arriving in Luoyang at 4:10 PM on the same day for an overnight stay. They will then depart from Luoyang at 8:00 AM the next morning, arriving in Peiping at 2:00 PM on the same day. At the same time, connections can be made in Luoyang with the Shanghai-Xinjiang route to Xi'an, Lanzhou, or Nanjing and Shanghai. Previously, traveling from Guangzhou to Peiping, Taiyuan, Luoyang, Xi'an, Lanzhou, Hankou, Changsha, and other places required ten days or more. Now, it only takes one and a half days.

Stipulated Flight Distances and Fares. According to the company's measured aerial distances, Peiping to Taiyuan is 450 kilometers, Taiyuan to Luoyang is 350 kilometers, Luoyang to Hankou is 500 kilometers, Hankou to Changsha is 300 kilometers, and Changsha to Guangzhou is 600 kilometers, making the total distance of the Peiping-Canton route 2,200 kilometers. Passenger fares are set at 60 yuan from Peiping to Taiyuan, 40 yuan from Taiyuan to Luoyang, 50 yuan from Luoyang to Hankou, 50 yuan from Hankou to Changsha, and 150 yuan from Changsha to Guangzhou, making the total fare for the Peiping-Canton route 350 yuan. This fare is significantly lower than that of the Shanghai-Xinjiang route, as the cost of gasoline used in stations west of Xi'an on the Shanghai-Xinjiang route is more than three times higher than that on the Peiping-Canton route, resulting in different costs.

Large Aircraft Will Be Used. According to General Manager Li, the Peiping-Canton route will temporarily use the existing Junkers W.34 aircraft with 575 horsepower, so the journey from Guangzhou to Peiping temporarily requires one and a half days. To make flights between Peiping and Canton even faster, the company has ordered a Junkers Ju 52 large aircraft from Germany. It should arrive in China within three months at the latest. Once it arrives, this type of aircraft will be used. It is noted that this aircraft has not been seen in our country before. It is equipped with three 700-horsepower engines, totaling 2,100 horsepower. The aircraft's weight is 5,400 kilograms, with a payload of 3,800 kilograms. It can carry 30 passengers with exceptionally comfortable seating. The cruising speed is 230 kilometers per hour, with a range of over 1,400 kilometers. Once this aircraft arrives, Peiping and Canton can be reached in one day.
