Reports of China National Aviation Corporation Plane Sinking in Sea Increasingly Confirmed; Seat Cushion Recovered Near Xunshan Yesterday; Reports of Fuselage Discovery Were Misinformation 139

Shen Shi News Agency reports that after China National Aviation Corporation Flight 17 went missing, newspapers yesterday reported that the plane's keel had been found in the sea near the Seven Sisters Islands. The company immediately dispatched aircraft from Jiujiang and Wuchang to investigate. According to inquiries made by a Shen Shi News Agency reporter, the report of the fuselage being discovered is completely inaccurate. However, one of the plane's seat cushions was continuously retrieved from the sea. The details are as follows:

One Seat Cushion Continues to be Found. Three people dispatched by the company were led by fisherman Zhang Huixi, who found the wreckage, to continue the search along the coast of Jintang Gorge near Huangmang Mountain yesterday morning. Yesterday afternoon, a telegram was received stating that a rubber seat cushion from the missing plane was netted in the sea off Xunshan.

Other items and the fate of the victims remain to be determined. However, based on the seat cushion and previously obtained mailbags, it is generally inferred that the plane sank into the sea, which is now almost certainly confirmed.

Report of Fuselage Discovery is Completely Inaccurate. Reports that the entire missing plane had been found near the Seven Sisters Islands are completely inaccurate, according to the person in charge of the company. Since the company offered a reward of 500 yuan, fishermen in the area have been actively searching and often making reports that are not entirely accurate. Yesterday morning, the company received a letter from the Yuyao Salt Affairs Weighing and Releasing Bureau stating that on the 29th day of the lunar month, fishermen saw an airplane descending from the sky in the sea off Xinpu. They intended to provide assistance, but due to the large waves, they were unable to do so. In a split second, the plane disappeared. However, according to the company's map investigation, there is no place called "Xinpu." Whether this is a misunderstanding is still under investigation. The discovery of the seat cushion today makes the theory that the plane sank into the sea more reliable, but it is still difficult to determine where it sank.

Board Meeting to be Held Today. In addition to ordering new aircraft from the United States, the company will hold a board meeting at 5:00 PM today to discuss future aviation safety issues, report on the loss of the plane, and sign the new contract for purchasing aircraft. When the two new Commodores arrive in Shanghai, the original Shanghai-Canton route can be fully restored. The company is currently planning to improve facilities along the route to ensure the safety of travel when flights resume in the future.

Ministry of Transportation Stipulates the Number of Crew Members on Various Ships; Yesterday, the Maritime Administration Bureau was Instructed to Comply 141

Da Gong News Agency reports that because the number of crew members on various ships has never been regulated, leading to arbitrary standards, which is deeply related to the shipping industry, the Ministry of Transportation has recently formulated measures for the number of crew members employed on ships and issued a general order to maritime administration bureaus in various places to instruct their subordinates to comply. The Shanghai Maritime Administration Bureau also received a notice yesterday. The details are as follows:

Ministry of Transportation Instructions. The Ministry of Transportation instructed the Shanghai Maritime Administration Bureau yesterday: "Upon investigation, the number of crew members on ships is mostly regulated by law in various countries in the East and West. Our country has not yet formulated such laws, causing the number of crew members employed on ships to be arbitrary, making management difficult for the competent authorities. The Maritime Administration Department of this Ministry has drafted a table of the number of crew members on ships and submitted it to the current meeting to promote the shipping industry for joint discussion. The meeting unanimously agreed to request the Ministry to issue a general order for implementation. In the future, all ocean-going, coastal, and inland river ships should immediately comply with the listed numbers and employ crew members. In addition to separate orders, a copy of the table of the number of crew members on ships is enclosed for compliance and to instruct your subordinates to comply. This order." It is heard that the bureau has already instructed various shipping companies to take note.

Number of Crew Members. The Ministry of Transportation's table of the number of crew members is as follows: (1) Ocean-going routes: For ships of 1,600 tons or more, there must be one captain, one chief mate, one second mate one third mate, one Chief Engineer, one first assistant engineer, one second assistant engineer, and one third assistant engineer. (2) Coastal or near-sea routes: For ships of 500 tons or more but less than 1,000 tons, there must be one captain, one chief mate, one Chief Engineer, and one first assistant engineer. For ships of 1,000 tons or more but less than 3,000 tons, there must be one captain, one chief mate, one second mate, one Chief Engineer, one first assistant engineer, and one second assistant engineer. For ships of 3,000 tons or more, there must be one captain, one chief mate, one second mate, one third mate, one Chief Engineer one first assistant engineer, and one second assistant engineer, and one third assistant engineer. (3) Inland river routes: For ships of 50 tons or more but less than 200 tons, there must be one captain and one Chief Engineer. For ships of 200 tons or more but less than 500 tons, there must be one captain and one Chief Engineer. For ships of 500 tons or more but less than 1,000 tons, there must be one captain, one chief mate, one Chief Engineer, and one first assistant engineer. For ships of 1,000 tons or more but less than 3,000 tons, there must be one captain, one chief mate, one second mate, one Chief Engineer, one first assistant engineer, and one second assistant engineer. For ships of 3,000 tons or more, there must be one captain, one chief mate, one second mate, one third mate, one Chief Engineer, one first assistant engineer, and one second assistant engineer, and one third assistant engineer.

Central Government Promulgates Supplementary Measures for the Organization of Shipping Associations 142

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce issued a notice to the city's shipping industry, inland river shipping industry, civil shipbuilding industry, coal and stone barge industry, sand ship industry, and other trade associations: "We hereby inform you that on the 18th of this month, we received a letter from the Shanghai Special Municipal Executive Committee of the Kuomintang of China, stating that according to Document No. 6282 from the Mass Movement Guidance Committee of the Central Executive Committee, the organization of shipping associations should be based on the Trade Association Law of Industry and Commerce, which was previously communicated by the former Central Training Department. Subsequently, shipping merchants in various places submitted that the business nature of shipping merchants differs greatly from that of general merchants, and the general regulations for merchant organizations cannot be fully adapted to shipping merchants with special characteristics. In order to thoroughly remedy this situation, this committee, together with the Ministry of Transportation and the Ministry of Industry, drafted supplementary measures for the organization of shipping merchants and forwarded them to the Central Government for review and submission to the National Government for promulgation and implementation. Now, the draft measures have been resolved by the 399th meeting of the Central Political Conference to 'pass and send to the National Government' and were promulgated by the National Government on March 21. In the future, matters concerning the organization of shipping merchants should be handled in accordance with these measures and the Trade Association Law of Industry and Commerce. In addition to separate letters, we enclose a copy of the supplementary measures for the organization of shipping merchants for your information and to instruct your subordinates to take note, etc.' Accordingly, we enclose a copy of the original document for your information, etc. sincerely." The supplementary measures for the organization of shipping merchants are recorded as follows: (1) All shipping or civil ship companies and firms should organize trade associations and join chambers of commerce in accordance with the Trade Association Law of Industry and Commerce and the Chamber of Commerce Law. (2) Shipping or civil ships that have not established companies or firms but have formally registered with the government may use their brand name as a unit to participate in trade associations. (3) The area of shipping or civil ship trade associations, in addition to the provisions of the Trade Association Law of Industry and Commerce, if the routes of each company or firm span two or more provinces, counties, and cities, the company or firm should join the trade associations in each location where the company or firm is located. If the company or firm has head and branch offices, they should also join the trade associations in each location separately. If there are fewer than seven companies in the area, and those that have not established companies or firms may join the trade associations in the counties and cities through which the route passes. (4) The highest supervisory authority of shipping or civil ship trade associations is the Ministry of Transportation. In addition to matters concerning establishment, dissolution, and organization of association affairs, which should be submitted to the local government and forwarded to the Ministry of Transportation for approval and sent to the Ministry of Industry for record, major matters concerning shipping administration should be submitted directly to the Ministry of Transportation for approval.

The Ministry of Transportation replied to the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce and the Ningbo Fellow-Villagers Association yesterday: (Omitted above) Upon investigation, the postal service is a state-run enterprise, which is a common practice in countries around the world. The postal regulations of our country also stipulate this clearly, and it is inappropriate to forcibly compare it with the examples of ships and railroads. The National Transportation Conference in 1928 resolved that "all private postal bureaus should be abolished uniformly by 1930." This should have been implemented on schedule. Such delays have been going on for several years. If this continues and strict measures are not taken, the postal regulations will never be fully implemented, and the postal service will never be unified. The Directorate General of Posts previously reported the situation of private postal bureaus to the Ministry. In order to unify the postal service, the Ministry specifically instructed the Directorate General to strictly order all private postal bureaus to gradually cease operations by the end of 1934. In addition, it requested the Executive Yuan to issue a general order to military, political, and police agencies in all provinces and cities to assist in the crackdown, to close them all within the Ministry's specified time limit and not to extend it. This case has been approved and ordered to be implemented. Since this case has been approved for scheduled closure, it is difficult to extend it again. We hereby reply to the previous situation in the telegram.

Ministry of Railways Explains Punishment Law for Passengers Carrying Contraband 144

The Two Roads Administration received instructions from the Ministry of Railways yesterday explaining the penalty measures for passengers carrying contraband. The text of the order is recorded as follows: "According to the request from the Tianjin-Pukou Railway Administration Committee for an explanation of Article 16 of the passenger transport regulations for compliance, after investigation, passengers carrying dangerous goods, objectionable goods, or contraband should be handled in accordance with Article 16 of the regulations, depending on the severity of the case. For minor cases, in addition to a fine of no more than 100 yuan, the dangerous goods or objectionable goods may be returned to the passenger. If the case is considered serious or involves government bans, the persons and items involved should be sent to the competent authorities for handling. In addition, the phrase 'to the railway area or entrusted to the railway for transport' in the article includes the starting station, intermediate stations, and arrival stations. If passengers carry dangerous goods, objectionable goods, or contraband, whether at the starting station, intermediate station, or arrival station, in short, once discovered within the railway area, they should be handled in accordance with the provisions of the article. As for the phrase 'if losses or injuries occur due to carrying the above-mentioned items, the passenger must be responsible for compensation,' the meaning of the word 'carrying' refers to the passenger's luggage, suitcases, packages, etc., whether carried on their person or transported in the baggage car, are all items carried by the passenger and should be handled in the same way in accordance with the article. In addition to the three points listed above, you should immediately comply with them. The original text of the first half of Article 16 of the passenger transport regulations, 'Passengers carrying dangerous goods, objectionable goods, or contraband to the railway area or entrusted to the railway for transport shall be fined no more than 100 yuan or sent to the competent authorities for handling in accordance with the law,' should be amended to 'Passengers who carry dangerous goods, objectionable goods, or contraband into the railway area without authorization or hide them in luggage, packages, etc. and entrust them to the railway for transport shall be fined no more than 100 yuan, and when necessary, the persons and items involved may be sent to the competent authorities for handling in accordance with the law.' In addition to instructing the Tianjin-Pukou Railway Administration Committee to comply, we enclose the original submission of the committee for compliance. This order."

Tax Exemption for Peanut Kernels and Peanut Oil Transshipped Through Qingdao for Two Years; Implementation Begins Tomorrow to Save the Production and Sale of Miscellaneous Grains 146

European and American countries purchase a large amount of peanut kernels, soybeans, miscellaneous grains, etc. from our country every year. In the past, they were mostly transshipped from Shanghai for export. Since the fall of the Northeast, the situation has changed drastically. Soybeans, peanut kernels, and oils from the Northeast are no longer shipped to Shanghai, and the transportation rights are mostly controlled by the Japanese, which has a great impact on the late export industry. In order to save the miscellaneous grain export market, the Qingdao authorities have taken measures to exempt and reduce taxes. The details of this matter are reported as follows:

Japanese Merchants Control Miscellaneous Grain Exports. Before the loss of the Northeast, our country's peanut kernels, soybeans, soybean cakes, and peanut oil were shipped to England, Germany, the Netherlands, France, the United States, and Southeast Asia in large quantities. Most of them were transshipped in Shanghai. Since the September 18th Incident and the loss of the Northeast, these goods are no longer shipped to Shanghai, and the transportation of miscellaneous grains to Europe and America has been controlled by the Japanese. They have mostly switched to shipping from Dalian. Nippon Yusen, Osaka Shosen, Kawasaki Kisen, Dalian Kisen, and other companies have dispatched ocean liners to directly transport them, not only reducing our country's tax revenue but also greatly affecting the export of miscellaneous grains from various ports in our country.

Harmful to the Production and Sale of Various Places in the Country. Soybeans alone have been seized by Japanese shipping companies at a rate of 400,000 to 500,000 tons per year.

And the peanut kernels, peanut cakes, peanut oil, etc. that Southern China, such as Shantou, Xiamen, Guangzhou, has always purchased from the Northeast are also considerable. After the September 18th Incident, transportation was cut off, and Chinese shipping companies suddenly lost the transportation of this large cargo. Miscellaneous grain merchants in Guangdong, Shantou, and other places have purchased from Haizhou and other places to make up for the shortfall. However, recently, the Japanese puppets have a plan to sell soybeans, peanut kernels, etc. from the Northeast, on the one hand, demanding our country to open traffic, on the other hand, using Japanese ships to directly transport them to various places in Southern China and sell them at depreciated prices. This move has a great impact on the production and sale of miscellaneous grains in our country.

Qingdao Implements Transshipment Tax Exemption. Qingdao produces a lot of peanut kernels and peanut oil. Now, in order to save the markets in Southern China and prevent them from being seized by others, the Qingdao authorities have specially agreed with the Jiao Customs that peanut kernels and peanut oil shipped from the port and transshipped through Qingdao will be exempt from transshipment tax for two years from April 21. At the same time, the dock dues will also be completely waived, and the inspection fee for the goods will also be reduced by half from this date, all for a period of two years, to encourage exports. A notice was issued to all Chinese and foreign shipping companies that not only would goods transported to various ports in the country be tax-exempt, but peanut kernels and peanut oil transported to Europe and America from the area would also enjoy the benefits of tax exemption and fee reduction. There is now a large amount of peanut kernels and peanut oil stored in the port. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company will dispatch ships to Qingdao to transport 15,000 packages of peanut kernels to various places in Southern China, and foreign shipping companies will also compete to change to Qingdao for loading and transporting peanut kernels.

New Shanghai Municipal Council Held First Meeting Yesterday 147

The newly elected Shanghai Municipal Council for the 1934-1935 term held its first meeting at 4:30 PM on April 19. The councilors elected Mr. H.E. Arnhold as Chairman and Mr. B.G.-Gen. E.B. Macnaghten as Vice-Chairman. Mr. Arnhold immediately took office as Chairman and thanked the councilors for their support.

Mr. Arnhold was elected as a councilor in 1928 and served as a member of the Works, Vehicles, and Music Committees. In 1929, he was elected as Chairman and resigned in March of the following year. In 1932, he was elected as Vice-Chairman and served as a member or Chairman of the Finance, Police, and Public Utilities Committees. In 1933, he was elected as Vice-Chairman and also served as a member or Chairman of the Finance, Police, and Public Utilities Committees.

Guild of Gauze Band Industry Sends Letter to Various Groups, Requesting Attention to Japanese Goods 149

New Voice News Agency reports that the Preparatory Committee of the National Gauze Band Factory Industry Guild, due to the recent discovery of a large quantity of Japanese gauze bands in the city, which has severely impacted the industry, convened an emergency meeting on the 13th of this month. As a result of the discussions, several methods were decided upon to distinguish between domestic and Japanese goods for users. For example, all factory members of the guild who are salespeople must wear badges when doing business outside, and the trademarks must be stamped with the certificate of domestic goods issued by the guild to avoid mixing with Japanese goods. Since the news of this measure spread, Japanese gauze bands have been closely scrutinized by various stores. Therefore, Japanese gauze band merchants, realizing that their conspiracy has been exposed, were greatly alarmed and immediately sought countermeasures. It is reported that they held a banquet at a certain restaurant yesterday, inviting shameless merchants and so-called "utilized" Chinese salespeople to design a plan to continue their invasion. Ice Retailers Petition the City Party Headquarters Yesterday, Opposing Collusion Between Competitors and Japanese Merchants to Monopolize the Market 150

The Public News Agency reports that recently, Fu Zhiqing, the manager of the Japanese-owned Oriental Ice Factory, Gu Fuxiang of the Hygiene Company, and Gao Abing, Hu Huiqing, and Xiao Acai, among others, organized the "Xiecheng Company" on Hankou-Wallis Road, monopolizing the sale of all ice products from various factories, thus monopolizing the market and manipulating ice prices. The ice retailers, unable to withstand the oppression of Japanese merchants, organized a delegation to seek solutions. The details are as follows:

Industry Conference The ice retailers, in order to respond to the manipulation of Japanese merchants, convened a meeting of representatives from all ice retailers in Shanghai on the afternoon before yesterday to discuss countermeasures. More than 100 representatives attended the meeting. Qiu Haitao chaired the meeting, and it was decided to petition party and government agencies, as well as the Chamber of Commerce and the Citizens' Association, and to issue a declaration requesting assistance from all sectors of society.

Petition to the Party Headquarters Yesterday morning at 9:00 AM, Qiu Haitao, Wang Fengshan, Tang Abing, and others led more than 100 representatives to petition the City Party Headquarters. Zhu Longkui received them. The representatives' demands were: (1) to stop factories from signing contract agreements with Xiecheng Company; (2) to restore previous operations and prevent market monopoly. Mr. Zhu provided a detailed response, which the ice retailers found satisfactory before returning. It is reported that they plan to petition the Municipal Government's Social Affairs Bureau, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the Citizens' Association, and other organizations today.

Petition to Stop Collusion The petition to the party and government to stop the collusion stated: "Petition to stop collusion with Japanese merchants to monopolize the market, manipulate ice prices, vigorously oppress vendors, and exploit users; requesting prompt cessation to benefit sales." "We, the petitioners, are small-capital vendors in Shanghai who sell various types of ice. In the past, we operated with free competition, and although profits were small, ice prices were consistently balanced, forming a unified body of manufacturers, vendors, and consumers without disputes. Unexpectedly, the Japanese-owned Oriental Ice Factory (established by Japanese, managed by Fu Zhiqing), Gu Fuxiang of the Hygiene Company, and Gao Abing, Hu Huiqing, and Xiao Acai, among others, have been manipulated by Japanese capitalists to organize Xiecheng Company, which exclusively packages and sells all ice factory products, intending to monopolize the market, manipulate ice prices, vigorously oppress vendors, and exploit users. We, the petitioners, are unable to directly order and sell from the factories and unwilling to be oppressed by Japanese capitalists. Therefore, we request prompt cessation of all ice factories from entering into exclusive packaging and sales contracts with Xiecheng Company to benefit sales, avoid being monopolized, manipulated, oppressed, and exploited, and maintain the livelihood of the masses. This would be truly virtuous."

Armed Soldiers of the Public Security Team in Zhabei Have a Conflict with Bus Employees Over Riding Without Tickets - Armed Comrades Have a Dispute with Bus Employees - Three Company Employees Seriously Injured, Arousing Public Outrage 153

Yesterday at around 5:00 PM, in the jurisdiction of the Second Sub-Bureau of the Seventh District of Zhabei,

A conflict arose on Xiangyin Road between soldiers of the Public Security Team and the Huashang Public Bus Company over the purchase of tickets. As a result, three bus company employees were beaten and seriously injured, arousing the public outrage of all the company's staff. They expressed that if there is no fair resolution, a strike may occur. The details of the incident are as follows:

The Issue Begins 154

The Huashang Public Bus Company's Route 4 runs from the North Station to the Municipal Government. After the route was opened, conflicts occurred from time to time with public officials regarding riding the bus, so it was temporarily suspended. At that time, Mayor Wu Tiecheng, in order to actively promote the prosperity of the city center, issued Bulletin No. 53 on October 20, 1932, announcing that all military and police personnel, regardless of who they are, must purchase tickets in accordance with the rules when riding the public bus, in order to alleviate the difficulties of businesses and benefit the municipality.

Riding Without Tickets 155

Yesterday at around 5:30 PM, the Public Bus No. 4933 on Route 4 arrived at the entrance of the Animal Husbandry Company on Xiangyin Road. The company's inspector, Qian Yabing (a 22-year-old local), boarded the bus to check tickets.

At that time, he saw a soldier in the uniform of the Public Security Team without a collar badge who had not purchased a ticket. The inspector then instructed him to purchase a ticket. Unexpectedly, the soldier not only refused to purchase a ticket but also spoke harshly. The two sides were in a stalemate, and the bus stopped. Many passengers who looked like students rose up in protest and questioned the soldier, resulting in a conflict.

Conflict Occurs Seeing the group questioning him, the soldier became enraged and pulled the inspector off the bus. At that time, three soldiers from the same team happened to be standing there. Seeing their comrade being insulted, they all took off their waist belts and planned to encircle and beat Qian. Seeing this, another ticket inspector, Zhang Meilun (a 28-year-old from Xinhui, Guangdong), quickly got off the bus to protect him, but was no match for the four soldiers. Zhang's left eye and left arm were seriously injured. The nearby area was in chaos. In the midst of the chaos, Zhang Tingrong, an employee of the Municipal Government's Intelligence Department, happened to pass by and quickly ordered them to stop. Seeing the inspector injured, he called the nearby police and took both parties to the Second Sub-Bureau of the Seventh Department.

Second Dispute At the same time, Captain Zhou of the Third Battalion of the First Regiment of the Public Security Department heard the news and immediately joined the mediation, admitting fault and apologizing. Unexpectedly, one wave subsided, and another rose. When the last bus, No. 4932, on the route returned to the factory at 7:15 PM, more than 20 burly men wearing plain clothes and military pants blocked the bus. Huang Riguang, a timekeeper from Guangdong, happened to be riding the bus back to the company after finishing his shift. Without asking the reason, the crowd dragged Huang down and beat him severely.

Seriously Injured The second incident occurred at the entrance of the Second Sub-Bureau of the Seventh District. Seeing the situation was bad, the employee quickly fled to the sub-bureau for refuge but was pushed out by the guard, making it impossible to escape. As a result, his head and waist were seriously injured. Wang Shuyun (a 20-year-old from Taicang) and Zhu Azhao (a 32-year-old from Nantong), were also caught in the crossfire. At the same time, the company heard the news and urgently notified the Zhabei Firefighting Joint Association to send ambulances to take the injured to Tongren Hospital for treatment first, and then to Renji Hospital at night. Among the injured, Huang Riguang and Zhang Meilun were the most severely injured. Zhang's left arm was broken, and Huang was said to have stab wounds. It is now reported that all the company's staff are very angry and have expressed that if there is no fair resolution, they will all go on strike to show their determination.

Ten Years of Love, a Fleeting Dream - A White-Haired Old Man Abandons a Beautiful Woman - A Certain "Love You to the End" Now How is it? - A Bunch of Letters with Extremely Sweet Titles - Yao Lifen Sues Pang Chunshan in Court 156

Pang Chunshan, a wealthy merchant from Suzhou residing in Shanghai, is 67 years old and has many children and grandchildren. He currently resides at No. 48 Changyun Lane, Xinda Gulou Road. Pang used to be the manager of the Gongmao Salt Shop in the city and accumulated considerable wealth. In recent years, he founded the Yongheng Refined Salt Company and resigned from his position as manager of Gongmao. In the autumn of 1923, when Pang was still working at Gongmao, he met Yao Lifen when purchasing diamond jewelry for his family. At that time, Yao was 19 years old and had exceptional beauty. Pang wanted to take her as a concubine, so he hired Zhang Mingshan, a salesman at Gongmao, to act as a matchmaker. Yao was very willing.

Devoting herself to service, she began living with him. Soon after, she became pregnant and explained the situation to her mother. Her mother, seeing that the situation was irreversible, did not obstruct her and allowed her to go with Pang. Pang treated her well, and they always went together when he traveled, inseparable. Although it was a white-haired old man and a beautiful woman, their love was like fish and water. Unexpectedly, it has suddenly turned to ice, and Pang abandoned her like a worn-out shoe. Yao had a daughter at a young age, who is now 11 years old. Having been abandoned midway, the mother and daughter find it difficult to make a living. Therefore, she hired a lawyer to file a lawsuit against Pang Chunshan for

cohabitation and alimony, requesting the court to order the defendant to pay a one-time alimony payment of

10,000 yuan and a 5,000 yuan for the girl's education expenses. Yesterday afternoon, Shen Hong, a judge from the First Special District Court, held a hearing. The defendant was not present. According to the plaintiff Yao Lifen, "I am 30 years old, a local, and currently live with my mother on Xinzha Road. In July 1923, the defendant ordered Zhang Mingshan to purchase diamond jewelry from me, which I delivered. That's how I met the defendant. At that time, I was 19 years old, and the defendant was already over 50 years old. However, Zhang Mingshan, when acting as a matchmaker, concealed ten years of his age and based on what the defendant said

that his wife was dead, I agreed. We started living together first. It was in October that I told my mother about my pregnancy. We chose a lucky day and got married at Taihe Garden. At that time, my family sent out invitations for a banquet, but the defendant took no action. The following year, on June 16, I gave birth to a daughter at No. 48 Shanhai Pass Road. During my confinement period, the defendant still did not stay overnight every night. When I asked him, he hesitated and could not speak. Later, I was told by the landlord of the second house that the defendant had a wife and already had

children and grandchildren. Afterwards, the defendant went to Hubei and Sichuan with me. He gave me 70 yuan for household expenses every month, which was increased to 80 yuan last year. Starting in January of this year, he suddenly stopped giving me money, so I filed a lawsuit," etc. The defendant's representative lawyer defended the defendant, saying that the defendant's acquaintance with the plaintiff was purely for fun and there was no marital relationship. The girl can only be regarded as an adopted daughter, not his biological daughter. The plaintiff's lawyer argued that since the defendant treated the plaintiff as a plaything, it shows that today's abandonment is because he is tired of playing with her. This kind of behavior is truly

disrespectful to women and submitted a bunch of letters as evidence, saying that these were all letters from the defendant to the plaintiff, calling the plaintiff "dear sister," "dear concubine," or "dear wife," and even praising the plaintiff as a "woman of courage" and saying that he would "love her to the end." This not only proves that there is indeed a marital relationship between the two parties, but also shows the attitude of the defendant in the past, etc. Judge Shen then adjourned the hearing and ordered the defendant to be summoned for further questioning.

Unbelievable Methods of Hiding Heroin - Small Holes Found at the Bottom of Oranges - Cigarette Tobacco Removed from Cigars - Toothpaste Tubes and Bottoms of Baskets Everywhere 158

Yan Chongwen and Wang Xianian, police officers of the First Squad of the Water Patrol Team of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau, were patrolling the river on a patrol boat at around 2:00 PM the day before yesterday. When passing the Tai Mei Wharf on Lan Road, they saw a barge moored there. They immediately jumped onto the boat to check the passengers for smuggled contraband. They saw a woman in the cabin carrying a net basket, so they went forward to search it. They saw that the basket contained daily necessities such as toothpaste, but there were eleven oranges with dry, charred peels,

obviously purchased many days ago. They didn't know why the woman was still keeping them in the basket, so they became suspicious. They took one and examined it carefully. Suddenly, they found a small hole at the bottom of the orange. They smelled it and noticed a strange odor. They used their bayonet to cut it open and discovered that the inside of the orange was hollow and secretly contained heroin. They cut open the remaining oranges one by one and saw that each orange had the same small hole, filled with the above-mentioned drugs. They thoroughly examined the other items in the basket and found two boxes of cigars, but the middle of each cigar was also empty. All the tobacco had been removed and replaced with white heroin. There was also a tube of toothpaste, but what it contained was not toothpaste for brushing teeth, but the same drug. Then they searched the bottom of the basket and found four paper bags and nine cloth bags about a foot long, all filled with heroin. They detained the woman and took her and the赃物 back to the team, and transferred her to the Nanshi General Team. During the preliminary trial by Chief Zhu, the woman claimed to be Li Dongshi, 35 years old, from Sichuan. She used to work as a maid for the Mai family in the French Concession. The net basket was entrusted to her by Mr. Wang, whom she met on the ship, to take home and give to Mr. Mai. She didn't know that so many drugs were hidden inside and asked for forgiveness, etc. As the matter concerned the smuggling of contraband, she was ordered to prepare a document and, at around 1:00 PM yesterday, Li Dongshi, the eleven oranges, two boxes of cigars, one tube of toothpaste, four paper bags, nine cloth bags, and a large amount of heroin worth more than 1,000 yuan were transferred to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for interrogation.

Yang Xianmei, a 25-year-old woman from Liyang residing at No. 27 He Ping Li, Avenue Edward VII, Public Concession, has been working as a dance hostess at the Lafayette Garden Dance Hall in the French Concession for six months. At 3:30 AM on the 9th of this month, Yang had just finished dancing and was sitting next to the dance floor when Pan Meiying, a fellow dance hostess (22 years old this year, from Ningbo, residing at No. 172 Xinxin Lane, Dapu Bridge), also sat next to Yang and was eating her large dish. Because she used the knife and fork too forcefully, the soup in the shrimp bowl splashed out, splattering on Yang's light pink crepe dance dress. This dress had just been made and was worn for the first night. Being splattered with oily stains, she felt upset and questioned Pan. Pan stubbornly refused to admit it and spoke rudely, and they quarreled with each other. This has been briefly reported in the previous newspaper. After Yang's injury was examined, she hired lawyer Huang Xiubo as her agent and filed a lawsuit with the Criminal Court of the Second Special District Court against Chen Zhongqing, the manager of the Lafayette Dance Hall, and the two dance hostesses, Pan and Chen, accusing them of joint injury, requesting that they be investigated and punished according to law, and attaching a civil lawsuit to recover the 300 yuan loss of the jewelry lost due to the injury. Then, he asked, "What is the plaintiff Yang Xianmei accusing Chen Zhongqing and others of?" Yang replied that she was accusing them of injury, but Chen Cuqing, who was present, was actually mistaken. He was Chen Junying, the manager, and Chen Zhongqing was the accountant and had nothing to do with it. Chen Junying helped to beat and kick her. At this point, the plaintiff's agent, lawyer Huang Xiubo, said that since the name of the first defendant was wrong, he should be allowed to withdraw the part concerning Chen Zhongqing and submit a complaint to summon Chen Junying for questioning. The court approved it. Then, according to the plaintiff Yang Xianmei, "At 3:30 AM on the 9th, when the dance floor was about to close, Pan Meiying splashed soup on my clothes. When I questioned her, she scolded me and slapped me twice. Chen Aying came up to help and hit my arm. They went to the accounting room to tell the manager that I scolded them. Manager Chen Junying called me to the accounting room, scolded me first, told me not to come tomorrow, and then pushed me to the door and kicked me in the buttocks, causing me to fall to the ground unconscious. Later, I was helped up, and my diamond ring, platinum watch, and jade ring were all gone. I went outside, first to the police station, and then home. My face still has scars. I request that they be investigated and punished according to law." Then, the defendant Chen Aying testified, "I went to the accounting room to put on my coat. I saw Yang and Pan scolding each other. I went up to persuade them. Yang wanted to hit Pan but couldn't reach her, so she hit me instead. I really didn't hit her." The defendant Pan Meiying testified, "When I was eating shrimp, a drop of soup splashed on Yang Xianmei's clothes. I apologized to her, but she scolded me. Because it was a Sunday and there were many dancers, I didn't argue with her and went to tell the accounting room. Yang Xianmei went to the accounting room and slapped the table and scolded loudly. The accounting room told her not to come tomorrow. She slapped me, causing my earring to break. I really didn't hit her. Chen Aying was there to dissuade her. You can ask the Lafayette Dance Hall to investigate," etc. The official asked the plaintiff Yang Xianmei if she had any grudges against the defendants. Yang replied, "They never acknowledged me, so they deliberately bullied me." At this point, the official, seeing that the defendants were not all present, adjourned the hearing to the 26th for further questioning. Chen Zhongying's part was not accepted. The two defendants, Pan Meiying and Chen Aying, were ordered to be released on bail and await further instructions. During the trial of this case, relatives and friends of both parties, as well as the defendants' little sisters and rickshaw pullers, all came to the court to listen. The number of people in the audience was quite crowded.

Municipal Bureau of Public Works Actively Reorganizing Li Ma Road 164

The Municipal Bureau of Public Works considers Li Ma Road an important transportation artery in the Nanshi area. However, the demolition of houses obstructing the road has been delayed, causing delays in the construction period. The residents of the area have been notified to demolish and relocate according to the deadline. The announcement from the Bureau of Public Works is recorded below: Regarding the project of reorganizing the first phase of Li Ma Road, the obstructing houses that should be demolished have been repeatedly announced and urged to be demolished. Later, at the request of various shops along the road for a delay, and considering the difficult times, the deadline has been extended repeatedly, resulting in the road construction not being completed yet. Now, the municipal government's Order No. 9079 states that this case has been decided at the 255th municipal meeting, setting April 30th as the date for compulsory execution, ordering compliance. Therefore, an announcement is made, urging all owners, shops, and residents along the road within this section to comply and quickly move and demolish before the deadline, so that the bureau can start reorganizing the road. If there are further delays, the bureau will send workers to demolish on behalf of the residents, and the required labor costs will still be borne by the owners. Do not delay or hesitate, and do not misjudge the situation. This announcement is imperative.

Our office has repeatedly received letters from many members complaining that the profits from selling cigarettes are meager, and business is difficult due to competition among colleagues. This time, the price drops and bonuses offered by various tobacco companies have not benefited our small stores, resulting in significant losses. If you agree to our request, mutual feelings will be easily close, and both parties will benefit, avoiding misunderstandings and estrangements. In the future, if various companies have new domestic cigarettes to launch, and your association sends personnel to promote them, our colleagues should be happy to promote sales, etc. In addition to sending separate letters to the tobacco companies, we are sending a special letter to your association. This matter concerns the business of both parties, and we hope you will provide strong assistance. We are looking forward to your reply."

Further Hearing in the Gao Xiaochen-Tao Jiayao Debt Dispute Case 176

Gao Xiaochen from Xuzhou, represented by lawyer Liu Cailiang, filed a lawsuit against Tao Jiayao from Jiangxi in the Criminal Court of the Second Special Court. The case was heard again on the 16th by Judge Xu Shenjie in the Second Court, and the debate was postponed to May 1st. The lawyer Liu's defense recorded at the time had some discrepancies, so a further record is made below. The following is lawyer Liu's defense: The debt relationship in this case was transferred from the deceased Songhu Police Chief Xu Guobiao to the defendant. The defendant issued a promissory note as proof and paid interest for two years, which is an indisputable fact. The reason for the transfer, whether out of emotion or reason, does not need to be studied. What should be studied now is whether the promissory note held by the plaintiff, which was handed over to the defendant's relative Cao Boshan, was a fraudulent act. Whether it was fraud should be judged based on whether the Yuji Guangyutang share certificates, etc., handed over by Cao Boshan were completely true, and whether the meaning expressed was deceptive. Although these two share certificates were acknowledged by Wang Yaosheng, the general manager of Tongjisheng Salt Shop, a careful examination reveals that the 5,000 yuan Yuji share certificate is actually a temporary receipt of the shop, not a share certificate, which is already suspicious. Because the receipt was given on January 1st of the seventh year, while the 10,000 yuan Guangyutang share certificate was issued on January 1st of the eighth year, there is a gap of one year. Why was the share capital paid later? The stock has already been exchanged, but the receipt for the storage one year earlier is still in his hand, and he has not exchanged it. It can be seen that the defendant has not hidden the stock separately and deliberately confused the situation. That is, the defendant must have other entanglements regarding the previously paid share capital. Moreover, the later paid share capital has an interest payment booklet, but would the first paid share capital abandon its rights and never generate interest? Then, the defendant's use of the receipt as a stock certificate, and his concealment of the true facts, can be imagined. Even if we look at the Yuji invoice, the Tongjisheng Salt Shop is a partnership. According to commercial customs, the size of the shares and the rights and obligations must be stipulated in a contract agreement, signed by each shareholder, and each hold a copy as proof. This is a certain and unchangeable practice. Now, the defendant only has a stock certificate and no contract agreement as proof, and only the general manager Wang Yaosheng signed it. This stock certificate does not conform to commercial customs in essence, and it is difficult to recognize it as valid. Various loopholes cannot guarantee that it was not colluded with the defendant. Furthermore, concerning the interest booklet, from 1920 to 1926, the interest paid, except for 3,900 yuan in 1922, was 3,600 yuan in all other years. The so-called red interest refers to dividends and stock interest. The stock interest is either fixed at 8% or 1%, with a fixed interest rate. As for the dividend, it must be based on the amount of profit earned in the business as the standard for distribution. It cannot be the same every year. The interest paid on the interest booklet does not distinguish between dividends and stock interest, and it is neither more nor less, every year. In fact, there is no such coincidence. Moreover, according to the plaintiff's investigation in Tianjin at that time, the shop had suffered losses over the years since its opening and had never issued such high profits (this point will be presented after sending someone to Tianjin to investigate and verify). It can be seen that the interest booklet is also suspected of being untrue. If this booklet is considered true, the defendant has an income of more than 3,000 yuan on a 10,000 yuan share capital, which is more than 30%. The interest can also be said to be high. Now, the amount owed by the defendant to the plaintiff, excluding the 5,000 yuan that has been repaid, is only 15,000 yuan. The annual interest is only 8%, totaling 1,200 yuan. After deducting the overpaid interest, there is still a difference of more than 2,000 yuan. Even the most foolish person would be willing to sacrifice heavy interest to repay others. Based on the above, the receipt, stock certificate, and interest booklet are obviously untrue, and there is no concealment. Now, setting aside whether they are true or not, even if they are considered true, according to the letter from Wang Yaosheng, the general manager of Tongjisheng, this stock certificate is registered and he has a seal. If he wants to withdraw the capital and interest, Tao Guangyutang and Tao Yuji must be present to verify that the seal matches. Moreover, Tao Guangyutang is the name of Mr. Tao Xingru (the defendant's name). Xingru and his brother have been close friends for many years and have other relationships. Even if Mr. Xingru withdraws the capital and interest, we should notify our shop by letter, or contact us ourselves. There is no reason for others to handle it on his behalf. Even if there is a mortgage or transfer, it should be effective only after both parties agree and the name is changed. This kind of content and procedure should be well known to the defendant. The defendant knew that the shop was about to close down, and knew that it could not be transferred and the interest could not be withdrawn. He concealed the truth, falsely claiming that it could be transferred and the interest could be withdrawn. His act of making a false matter appear true and expressing it is called fraudulent behavior. The defendant used fraudulent behavior to cause the plaintiff to be mistaken, handing over the original promissory note to Cao Boshan, and took the opportunity to avoid debt and obtain illegal property benefits. He is obviously in violation of Article 363, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Law. Therefore, he filed a self-lawsuit and attached a civil suit, requesting that the defendant be punished according to law. As for the civil suit, he requested the return of the principal of 15,000 yuan, and 8% annual interest from July 1925 until the end of the execution.

Brush Factory on Xuegong Street Suffers Fire; Landlord and Tenant Shift Blame for the Fire 177

At 8:30 yesterday morning, a fire suddenly broke out on the upper floor of the Zhang Rongxing brush factory, opened by Zhang Guirong from Huai'an at No. 10, Lane 7, Yuhou Li, Xuegong Street, Wenmiao Road, Nanshi. In a short time, the flames were fierce and broke through the roof. When the fire brigades of the West District and others learned of this, they quickly drove seven fire trucks to the scene. After the firefighters' best efforts to extinguish the fire, it was finally extinguished after about an hour. The fire destroyed the double-section shikumen house at No. 10 and spread to the single-section shikumen house at No. 9 next door, totaling seven households. The loss of property was quite large. At that time, the surrounding neighbors moved and robbed each other's belongings, causing chaotic order. The Second Squad of the Second Precinct of the Municipal Public Security Bureau sent police to suppress the situation and investigate the cause of the fire. According to the second landlord, Zhang Ronggui, the fire was caused by Zhang Wang, a widow from Qingjiang, who went to the stocking factory to work, leaving only her two daughters, aged ten and seven, at home who started the fire while cooking. However, according to Zhang Wang, her two daughters had not yet gotten out of bed when the fire broke out. Neighbors rescued them, and their clothes were not even put on yet. According to some people, the fire was caused by workers from the brush factory upstairs. Rumors were flying, and it was difficult to determine the truth. In the end, the precinct took both the second landlord Zhang Guirong and Zhang Wang to the precinct and transferred them to the headquarters for questioning.

Ye sent Xue to Renji Hospital for treatment and turned himself in to the Southeast Hospital outside Xiaoximen for treatment. However, Xue died in the hospital at 0:50 am on the 18th due to burns all over his body and heat attacking his heart. The hospital notified the police station, which sent detectives to send the body to the Tongren Fuyuan Branch Corpse Examination Office to request the Second Special Court to send personnel to identify the body. The body was claimed and coffined by the affiliated company. On the other hand, the police station sent detectives, together with detectives from the Public Security Bureau, to the Southeast Hospital the day before to take Ye back to the police station. Due to the unhealed injuries, he was sent to Guangci Hospital for treatment. Yesterday, the police station sent Ye's case transfer form to the Criminal First Court of the Second Special Court. Police station lawyer Fei Xizhen explained the case, indicting him for the crime of endangering public safety and requesting a postponement until the defendant's injuries have healed. Judge Tu核禀 approved the request for a postponement and will question the defendant when his injuries have healed.

Lu Jiye's "An Outline of Chinese Drama" Published 186

This book discusses Chinese drama, tunes, and legends of all dynasties. Letter to the Editor 193

To the Editor: After reading your newspaper and other newspapers' reports on April 18 (regarding the Duck Industry Turmoil) and the Chicken and Duck Association's unauthorized change to the 37% foreign exchange rate telegram to various ports, suspending the shipment of ducks to Shanghai, etc., we believe that the aforementioned content is purely one-sided from the duck industry and completely obliterates the facts of the current turmoil. Upon investigation, chicken and duck merchants act as agents for buying and selling on behalf of customers, and regardless of whether the foreign exchange rate is large or small, or whether it is in full silver dollars, the amount received and paid by both the customer and the seller is the same. They only have the right to collect commission and have no other gains or losses. The reason for the current turmoil is that after the January 28th Shanghai Incident, customers insisted on only selling in silver dollars due to the difficulty and danger of transporting goods. The merchants had no right to stop this due to the customer-merchant relationship, the interests of the customers, and the merchants' rights. At that time, the duck merchants fortunately agreed, and the merchants even temporarily sacrificed not collecting commission from the duck merchants, so all transactions were in silver dollars, which has been the case until now, for less than two years. Although the duck merchants repeatedly requested the restoration of the 37% foreign exchange rate based on the conditions signed with the merchants at the Social Affairs Bureau, the customers understood that the duck merchants were seeking an unexpected benefit. There is also no precedent for using large or small silver dollars for purchasing goods in various places in Jiangbei, and the current economic bankruptcy and suffering of the rural areas is severe. Therefore, they are determined not to yield. Despite repeated persuasion from merchants and market officials, there was no effect. It is said that they have already filed a petition with the authorities. The merchants are in a dilemma, which has led to the current suspension of the market. As for the reason for the suspension, it was first announced by the duck merchants, who stopped slaughtering on the 14th and refused to buy ducks from the merchants from that day forward. On the 13th, our merchants had several thousand ducks, but because no one inquired about them, they have all been transported to the duck ponds in Pudong for feeding. The facts are all there and cannot be concealed. Moreover, after the duck merchants issued the suspension order, a fellow merchant, Weng Azhi, privately slaughtered seven geese and was punished. Therefore, the market turmoil was actually started by the duck merchants, and our merchants cannot bear any responsibility. As for the telegram to various ports to suspend the shipment of ducks to Shanghai, because the duck merchants have already issued a suspension order and refuse to buy ducks at all, and have also organized a disciplinary team to patrol the market, if we continue to allow customers to ship ducks in large numbers, they will have no way to sell them, and the resulting delays, deaths, and losses will be huge. How can we maintain this? The telegram to suspend the shipment of ducks to Shanghai was indeed a last resort for the merchants and was also a legitimate procedure. As for Chairman Zhao Songge's statement that he forbade the sale of 37% foreign exchange rates and that some merchants were willing to sell them, this statement is not worth a knowing person's laugh. This matter not only concerns the sovereignty of the customers, but even if the merchants have sovereignty, it is a matter for the entire industry and cannot be manipulated by the opinion of one chairman. Therefore, we have sent this detailed letter and respectfully request that your editor uphold justice and publish this letter for correction. The entire industry will be grateful. Respectfully addressed to the Shen Bao, Shanghai Chicken and Duck Industry Association, April 18.

Reading Q&A

Clarification (Continued 2) - Reply to Mr. Xu Lezhen - 195

(11) What is the explanation of "The dynamic consciousness sees the guiding role"? (Page 26, line 12)

Answer: This means that "the scope of theory is not only to record existing things," "the most important thing is to transform the world," "to guide action." This passage criticizes the errors of the Spark faction, saying that although they have worked hard to describe the struggle process that is happening before their eyes, they are clumsy in the theory of guiding action. This statement refers to the Russian Social Democratic Party. To say that the party's dynamic consciousness has a guiding role, in other words, "the party" must not only have a correct grasp of the objective reality, but also make an explanation and description of the Russian revolutionary struggle process that was developing at that time. "The party" should dynamically (not passively) realize its guiding role in the development of the current objective situation, that is, not let go of the objective situation in the slightest, and most resolutely develop this situation, expand the conditions that are beneficial to oneself, and ruthlessly overcome the conditions that are unfavorable to oneself, instead of watching the situation and making some abstract dissections and explanations of the objective situation. Furthermore, it means to grasp the reality in a process, and consciously lead to the arrival of another new stage, instead of mechanically or opportunistically catering to the development of the objective world. I wonder if you fully understand this explanation? Now let's give another example to help you understand this.

For example, the current national crisis in China is known to everyone. What is the current situation? International imperialism has broken the Nine-Power Treaty and has moved from maintaining China's territorial integrity to recognizing a "puppet state," dividing up China. Naturally, this is unfavorable to China. However, what attitude should a political party take towards the current situation? It is not enough to merely make some dissections and explanations of this situation. Nor is it enough to simply cry out loudly and sing a lament of anger and violence once and be done with it. It should use the contradictions between the various imperialist powers that have created the recent international situation to subtly and resolutely destroy the conditions for the united attack on China by the imperialist powers, transform this unfavorable condition into one that is beneficial to itself, and thereby lead to a new situation, making this conspiracy of division impossible. However, this is not a question of abstract dissection and speculation, but of actively, consciously, and clearly understanding one's own leadership role and bearing the determination to assume this leadership. There is a famous saying that "history is made by mankind itself." That's right, every fact in every historical stage is developing objectively, and at the same time, people can consciously change it. The current national crisis in China is certainly serious, but this does not mean that the Chinese nation has no way out. I hope you can understand this!

(12) What is "historical materialism"?

Answer: "Historical Materialism" is called (Materialistic Conception of history) or "Materialism of History" ("Historical Materialism"). Materialist dialectics is a general methodology that can be applied to all phenomena in the universe. Historical materialism is the application of materialist dialectics in explaining social phenomena. Therefore, materialist dialectics is general, while historical materialism is special. Society is a special form of objective existence, so it has its own objective and special laws of development. The special laws of social development are: the production of means of livelihood and the exchange relations of produced goods are the basis of all social organization; the fundamental cause of all social changes and all political revolutions is not due to human understanding of justice or truth, but is the result of continuous reforms in production and exchange. Therefore, the driving force of social development is the change in productive forces. Productive forces always play their role under certain relations of production, and the social economic structure, the foundation of social life, is composed of these relations of production. All other social life is built on this foundation, so it is called "superstructure," such as politics, law, religion, morality, politics, etc. In order to suit the development of productive forces, the relations of production are constantly changing their content, but when the development of productive forces reaches a certain degree, when the existing relations of production cannot match it, then a conflict arises between the two, and then a social revolution occurs, destroying the old relations of production and establishing new relations of production. And all the old superstructures, because the foundation has fallen, will also change sooner or later. According to the special rules of development of the social economic structure, history can be divided into ethnic societies, feudal societies, capitalist societies, and socialist societies.

(13) "They do not doubt that the Soviet Union exists independently of their consciousness, they firmly believe that in daily practice, the Soviet Union really exists, and the proletariat's struggle for socialism really exists." These few sentences are too profound, please explain them simply. (Page 49, lines 10-11)

(15) "They did not want to consider society as a material process that exists independently of human will." The meaning is not very clear. (Page 50, line 5)

(16) "To make them know that capitalist society is an objective material process." The meaning is not very clear. (Page 51, line 6)

Answer: The nature of these three questions is almost the same. Probably Mr. Xu is not clear about the fundamental concept of materialism, and that is why these questions arise. In the answer to question 9, we have already said some of the fundamental concepts of materialism. Perhaps Mr. Xu will understand after reading them. That is, materialists believe that the universe is composed of many materials, and these things exist independently of us. The 13th question, "The Soviet Union exists independently," means that this early socialist country is indeed a thing in the world and is not "their" fantasy. The 15th question is about the error of the "People's Party." The reason for their error is that they fell into the view of idealists and denied that society exists independently in the objective world, that is, the sentence you quoted. The 16th question is the same. The meaning of the sentence you quoted is that in the process of class struggle, the proletariat gradually knows that capitalist society is not the fantasy of a certain group of people, nor is it a theory, but it is indeed a thing in the objective world.

(14) What is "labor-moving class"? (Page 49, line 13)

Answer: The word "labor" is misprinted; it should be "labor" (勞).

After reading so many questions that Mr. Xu has after reading this book, we feel that you should not read this book now. However, dialectical materialism is something we should pursue, and we must not give up because of a minor setback. Therefore, we hope that you will read "The Modern Worldview" instead. Also, many terms cannot be looked up in dictionaries, such as the New Philosophy Dictionary and the Modern Language Dictionary. The above answers are also mostly excerpts from those dictionaries.

Key Points for Improving Education in Fujian Province: Report on Inspection by the Ministry of Education's Supervisor 197

The Ministry of Education previously dispatched Supervisor Tang Xifen to inspect education in Fujian Province. The results of the inspection have been reported to the Ministry. The following is a summary of the suggestions for improving education in Fujian Province:

1. It has been found that educational funding in the province accounts for only 12% of the total expenditure of the provincial government, which is less compared to other provinces. Efforts should be made to increase it, taking into account the need to promote educational undertakings in the province, with the goal of reaching the standard that the provincial government's educational funding should account for 20% of the total expenditure.

2. The provincial education budget should be divided into two categories: regular and temporary. After the regular expenses budget of provincial schools has been verified, compiled, and approved, except for using the surplus for equipment upgrades, there should be no phenomenon of using the funding for one class to operate two or more classes. For short-term provincial education projects and large expenditures for the construction and purchase of schools, a plan and estimate should be prepared separately before the year, collected for review, and a temporary expense budget table should be compiled, including a reserve fund item, which can be used to adjust regular expenses and prepare for temporary special expenditures. As for the monthly funding for provincial educational institutions, provincial and non-provincial institutions should be treated equally and paid at the same time.

3. The regulations for subsidies to private schools in counties should be revised, emphasizing the equality of secondary education opportunities in various places, promoting the development of vocational and normal education, and supervising the improvement of the performance of private schools in counties. The subsidy methods should be formulated according to the following principles: (1) The distribution standard of subsidies: vocational schools must account for 50%, normal schools 30%, and middle schools 20%. (2) The use of vocational school subsidies, in addition to being designated by the department to enrich vocational equipment, may also be used to subsidize the salaries of vocational subject teachers. (3) The use of normal and middle school subsidies is limited to the salaries of teachers of major subjects. (4) Counties with fewer middle schools but excellent performance should be subsidized first. (5) Private middle schools in counties with annual expenses of more than 4,000 yuan should be temporarily suspended from subsidies. (6) Subsidized schools must comply with the regulations and rules issued by the Ministry and Department regarding the school in question.

4. Efforts should be made to restore the management authorities of county and municipal education funds to avoid disruptions, and the Department should send personnel to conduct thorough investigations into their sources, distribution, and audits, and formulate rectification measures separately.

5. Private primary and secondary schools must collect various student fees in accordance with the regulations issued by the Ministry.

6. The private Fujian College lacks funds. In addition to provincial treasury subsidies and tuition fees, there are few other sources of funding for perennial expenses, which is not enough to sustain it. The organization of the board of directors is also unsound, school equipment is extremely scarce, and no achievements have been seen. It should be closed immediately or closed early, but no new students may be recruited in the future. The military training in the affiliated middle school does not comply with the Ministry's regulations and should be corrected.

7. The private Xiamen University has relatively complete construction and equipment, and the faculty and staff are also working hard. However, it lacks funds, and the perennial expenses exceed income by 10,000 yuan per month. In addition to the 5,000 yuan monthly subsidy from the Fujian Provincial Department of Finance and the 2,500 yuan monthly subsidy from the China Cultural Fund, which should continue to be allocated as usual, the school's board of directors should quickly raise sufficient funds to avoid instability. The normal school department of the affiliated high school should be ordered to stop recruiting students and close down in stages to comply with the law.

8. The funding for provincial vocational schools is still 7% less than the standard set by the Ministry. If secondary education funding increases in the future, it should be allocated to vocational schools first; otherwise, the funding for provincial normal schools and middle schools must be reduced and distributed accordingly. If the provincial vocational schools in the same location have the same departments, they should be merged. If the departments are not fully suitable for local production industries, equipment should be enriched, or the school site should be appropriately moved, or the school should be reorganized accordingly. The province's major production industries have shown signs of decline, but there is no vocational education to improve them. Vocational schools should be established immediately for industries such as fisheries, tea, and handicrafts.

9. There are currently only two county-run vocational schools. In addition to the four measures formulated by the Department for reorganizing county-run junior high schools into vocational or normal schools, the following principles should also be followed: (1) Select county areas with fewer vocational schools in the province's current vocational school areas for reorganization first. (2) Counties with more than two middle schools but no vocational schools should be reorganized first. (3) Counties with special major production but no vocational schools to improve them should be reorganized first.

10. Provincial normal school districts should be handled with reference to the following principles: (1) Each district should establish one normal school, one rural normal school, or one simple rural normal school. (2) If there are two or more schools of a normal nature in the same district, they must be established separately. (3) Districts with underdeveloped primary education and fewer large cities should establish rural or simple rural normal schools first. (4) Normal schools should be established independently. The normal school departments or classes attached to them should be independent immediately. (5) Each provincial normal school must have an affiliated primary school and run short-term primary school classes, two-part systems, or single-grade classes for teaching practice. (6) Provincial normal schools must enroll students from each county in the district according to a quota, taking into account the results. (7) The Provincial Department of Education should designate normal schools in each district to run summer training classes for primary school teachers to seek further education for primary school teachers.

11. Provincial middle school districts should be re-divided with reference to the following measures: (1) According to the principles set by the Ministry, "Senior high schools should be concentrated in several central locations. If there are two senior high school classes in the same location, the senior high school classes should be merged and established separately." and follow the normal vocational school district method, using the old Daoshu as the provincial senior high school district. (2) For the provincial junior high school, if there are many classes, for the convenience of management and training, a girls' junior high school should be established separately or the girls' high school classes should be merged into a girls' high school.

12. There are a total of nine provincial primary schools, which have been taken over by local education administrative agencies since the 23rd year, until the 25th year.

All provincial primary schools have been completely reorganized, and the original funding has been redistributed to run short-term compulsory education, and should be handled with reference to the following principles: (1) Provincial short-term compulsory education is to demonstrate quality and can set up one to several short-term compulsory primary schools in a county or district, and set up one instructor to guide it. (2) Counties and cities that have set up compulsory education experimental areas and short-term compulsory education experimental areas do not need to set up provincial short-term compulsory primary schools. (3) The location of the school should be chosen where there are more out-of-school children and no affiliated primary schools of various normal schools.

13. The use of the primary school subsidy funds allocated by the Department of Finance to each county must be distributed according to the following principles: (1) The use of subsidies is limited to compulsory education. (2) The distribution of subsidies to each school must be limited to the payment of salaries to qualified full-time teachers. (3) Counties that have not held compulsory education or have no qualified full-time teachers may have their subsidies retained by the Department of Education.

14. The use of the primary school subsidy funds allocated by the salt fund must be distributed according to the following principles: (1) The use of subsidies is limited to private junior primary schools and primary schools for the blind, deaf, and orphans. (2) The subsidized private schools must be truly excellent in performance, have financial difficulties, and have been verified and qualified. (3) Subsidies to private junior primary schools must pay attention to the distribution of their regions.

15. The Fuzhou Provincial Public School should be taken over by the Literacy Education Committee, and its original funding, together with the funding to subsidize public schools in various counties, should be redistributed to seek universality.

China College Basketball Team Wins First Game Against St. John's Yesterday: Score is 44 to 30, St. John's Leads by 2 Points in the First Half, China College to Play Jiaotong Today 213

The China College team, the basketball leader in Beiping, has come to Shanghai for a competition. The team has strong players such as Zhang Yucai, Wang Kanruo, and Duan Zhuo. In the first game last night, the team competed against St. John's University in Fanwangdu and won the victory. The score was 44 to 30, and the first half was 15 to 17, with St. John's leading. The following is a description of the game:

St. John's Took the Lead At the start, people crowded together. In the beginning, the game was unfamiliar to the team, and many tests did not succeed, and they inevitably felt flustered. Xu Wenkui and Zhou Xuexian, the left and right generals of St. John's, took the opportunity to advance, succeeding in one and then another, creating a priority situation of eight to zero. The China team then counterattacked. Duan Zhuo was unwilling to show weakness, and Zhao Zhenji followed, so they gradually caught up, eight to four, eleven to seven, and finally made it fifteen each. Special Article

The Current State of Secondary Education in England (Part 2) (5) Examinations 222

— Zhu Zhenrou

The goal of every British secondary school student upon enrollment is not graduation, but to pass the graduation examination. This examination is not administered by the school itself, but by an external organization (usually a university). This fundamental examination is called the Ordinary School Certificate, and it is as difficult as the university entrance examinations in other countries.

Every student taking the London University Ordinary School Certificate at the age of sixteen who passes the examination in five designated subjects can obtain a certificate of passing. This certificate is kept by the Ministry of Education and serves as the student's qualification for entering university or is accepted by various other professions as a substitute for their required professional examinations. Furthermore, this certificate is also an essential requirement for students who wish to work in banks, insurance companies, or other commercial sectors. Therefore, every student strives to obtain this certificate before leaving school.

(6) Enrollment

The average number of students enrolled in each secondary school in London is approximately four hundred and twenty-five. No secondary school enrolls more than one thousand students, although one secondary school has enrolled nine hundred. The standard enrollment quota is four hundred and fifty students. If this number is exceeded, the school authorities believe that the essential element of education—individual guidance—loses its effectiveness. Each school authority believes that teachers should personally provide individual guidance to each student, and at the same time, a friendly attitude and a spirit of continuous mutual discussion should be cultivated between teachers and students. This is a characteristic of secondary education in England.

In British education, social relationships and personal contact are considered particularly important. Restrictions are not only placed on students in the classroom, but also on group meals. For example, at the Universities of Cambridge and Oxford, all students must have at least one group meal a day; some universities even require two. Any student can choose not to live on campus, and breakfast and dinner are also optional, but lunch must be eaten together on campus. All British secondary schools have excellent dining hall facilities specifically for student group lunches. Some students bring lunch from home, and the school rents out bowls and utensils for a small fee. Other students' lunches are provided by the school, and the menu includes pork, bread, butter, milk, tea, and fruit, costing about nine pence per person. In central schools, the cost is only seven pence per person.

(7) School Calendar

In London, the number of school days per year is approximately forty-four weeks for primary schools, but only thirty-nine weeks are stipulated for secondary schools. These thirty-nine weeks are divided into three terms, each lasting three weeks. As for the remaining holidays, they are freely determined by the principal of each school, and no one may interfere. The most amusing point is that the central education authorities are often vaguely unaware of the dates and lengths of spring break or other holidays within each secondary school, because the holidays of each secondary school are not uniform.
