Records of the Lingering Fragrance 223

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of Qing, translated by Qin Shouou

Therefore, in these short few minutes, on this row of imperial trains ready to depart, although black smoke was similarly billowing from the chimneys and steam was similarly filling the boilers, not a single person was on board to attend to them; it was not until the Empress Dowager was settled in her own carriage that these stokers and drivers were able to climb up from the ground, return to their fixed positions, and await the order to depart.

During the twenty-odd days before we prepared to depart, we don't know how many difficulties arose, leaving Qing Shan almost exhausted! The first difficult problem was the train's crew... because the Empress Dowager insisted on having the eunuchs

take charge of the train's affairs, but how could that be done? Although most of the eunuchs had served in the palace for many years and were fully capable of serving as butlers or maids in ordinary families, they had never received any basic railway knowledge; how could they operate a train?

Qing Shan spent a great deal of effort persuading her to abandon this preconceived notion; but she finally firmly instructed that, in any case, no railway workers were allowed to come within her sight. This showed that she was still adhering to the ancient

dictum of not using men to serve her!

This problem was thus resolved, but other matters were not so easily dealt with. One of the most laughable was the Empress Dowager's firm command to Qing Shan to instruct all the train's crew, from the driver to the lowest-ranking cleaner, to all wear court boots, don court hats, and dress up as complete eunuchs. A Scene 224

— Chonghua

In the time before the movie starts, the movie theater displays a special social scene. For a small dispute, they argue without giving way to each other, as if the Chinese people are very spirited and absolutely cannot tolerate any bullying. This time, a student, for the sake of a seat, argued with a soldier in uniform. The student said: "This is my seat."

The soldier said: "What proof do you have?"

Thus, an ugly look gradually appeared on both sides' faces. The air in the movie theater suddenly became tense, and people stood up one by one to watch the excitement. The student certainly wanted to take advantage of this to show off completely in front of the public, and the soldier certainly did not want to appear as a weakling in front of so many people and step down in this way.

Just at this moment, suddenly there was a voice... "Don't quarrel! Are you Chinese?"

Turning their heads in surprise, it was a child who said it, still playing with orange peels in his hand.

I don't know if they didn't understand these words or if they disdained listening to the child's teachings, but they unexpectedly started fighting.

The child shouted again: "Save some strength to fight the Japanese."

However, they still ignored it.

I thought it was funny that they didn't know shame after being ridiculed by a child in this way.

Later, it was probably resolved by several black-clothed policemen who ran over.

Spoiling the Scenery 225

— Qingyun

This is indeed a great way to spoil the scenery, but the unconscionable Chinese people consider it insignificant, thus creating the same treatment as "Chinese and dogs" by foreigners!

In these few days, Suzhou's Tiger Hill seems like a young girl who has put on brilliant new clothes... The peach blossoms are as red as brocade, and the soft green willow branches are woven into lovely green oil curtains. The fragrant grass is also newly green like a lawn, filled with intoxicating allure everywhere. As a result, groups of spring excursion men and women are also flocking here to enjoy the spring. However, these elegant people, while leisurely touring the famous scenic spots, also want to carry out the elegant affair in the poem "when flowers bloom, pick them when you can," holding handfuls of mountain flowers as a special symbol of their spring outing. Those who come later can only look at the wooden sign that says "picking flowers and trees is prohibited," and sigh grandly!

Zhangjia Garden, along the Xiaohai River outside Changmen, is the private garden of the owner of Zhang Xiangfeng Confectionery, covering an area of about sixty acres. In addition to halls, pavilions, rockeries, ponds, etc., the garden is planted with various fruit trees, which has a unique poetic charm of boundless flat forests. In Suzhou's gardens, it occupies a unique charm. The Zhang family originally openly invites tourists to visit, which is originally the garden owner's unselfish intention. However, in recent days, a group of tourists has practiced the doctrine of plunder on the calligraphy and paintings of famous people and antique objects in the halls of the garden, completely stealing them. The Zhang family has suffered this loss and had to close the doors to those tourists who are not upper class.

Such a way to spoil the scenery may be regarded by a group of elegant people as a minor moral issue that is insignificant; however, the Chinese are equal to animals, but it is precisely on these minor moral issues that can be entered and exited!

As the saying goes: "One monk carries water to drink, two monks carry water to eat, three monks have no water to drink." People are generally lazy and want to be idle, but we should not shirk responsibility! Only by being hardworking, enduring hardship, and being diligent and responsible in handling affairs can we succeed in a great cause. 226

Small Talk

Research on Inkstones (26) Other Famous Inkstones 229

— Wuliao Ke

One person making two kinds of inkstones In the past, people imitated ancient inkstones, and they often made more than one kind. For example, the Song Dynasty's Liu Xisou, according to the Ou Spectrum, was good at making Chengni inkstones, but other books also say that Liu Xisou made excellent ancient tile inkstones, but they were not produced in large quantities, and scholars and officials' families could not have them readily available. Another example is the Ming Dynasty Jiangxi Prince, according to Tang's Inkstone Records, who was good at making Weiyang tile inkstones, but other books also say that the Prince made Bronze Sparrow inkstones, which had secret techniques, were rich and moist, and produced ink well. Those who obtained them regarded them as rare treasures. It can be seen that the Prince was actually imitating these two kinds of inkstones at the same time.

My late father, Lord Jinchuan, left behind a Bronze Sparrow tile inkstone, about seven inches long and slightly less than nine fen thick. The material is firm and fine, and it does not dry out the ink. The back has a coarse cloth pattern. There are six official script characters, "Made in the thirteenth year of Jian'an," in an ancient and vigorous style. On the upper right of the front, there are sixteen official script characters: "The essence of water and fire combines to form a shape." On the left, there are sixteen official script characters: "Heroes are gone, but tiles still remain." In the middle on both sides, there are twelve characters: "For the love of Tao Zhen's quality, it is appropriate to add the title of Jimo." Below, after checking previous people's notes, there are thirty-six official script characters: "I obtained it from the depths of the Zhang River, exchanging thirty-nine coins for it and adding it to my writing to be a plaything for erudition and love of art. Yuexian recognized it on the Double Ninth Festival of Hongwu Xinwei." These are horizontally arranged in eleven lines, with three or four characters per line. However, the lower end of my inkstone is already broken and cut off by four or five fen, so only one or two characters per line remain. For example, the characters "I, Zhang, Deep, Nine, And, Brush, For, Art, Xin, Wei, Yue" are still preserved, which is very regrettable. The Weiyang inkstone made by the Jiangxi Prince mentioned above has the three characters "Yuexian wrote," and this inkstone also has Yuexian's inscription. Therefore, it is suspected that this inkstone may also have been made by the Prince. However, I have never seen the real Weiyang inkstone made by the Prince, so it cannot be proven whether this inkstone was made by the Prince or was repeatedly imitated by someone else. It will be left to the appraisal of archaeologists.

Front

Fire Form For the Love of Country Hero Appropriate Jimo Title

Back

Attached Ancient Brick In addition to ancient tile inkstones, there are also ancient brick inkstones, and there are many fake products. According to the Yipiao Collection, ancient bricks, especially Han bricks, are the firmest. For example, Jianping bricks are from the time of Emperor Ai, Yongjian bricks are from the time of Emperor Shun, and Zhongping bricks are from the time of Emperor Ling. They all have a warm and moist color. It is said that at that time, when making bricks, the clay must be mixed for dozens of days, mixed with pine resin. Although the manufacturing method is slightly different from Chengni inkstones, the actual substance is roughly the same. After more than two thousand years, they are still lovely. Therefore, ancient brick inkstones were highly valued by inkstone enthusiasts in the Kangxi and Qianlong periods. Ruan Yuan of Yangzhou's Eight Obstacles Inkstone is the most famous, among which is a Yellow Dragon first year brick inkstone, which was later obtained by a Qing Taoist, who named his studio the Yellow Dragon Inkstone Studio. The love for it can be imagined.

Free Talk

New York Correspondence, Letter No. 1: New York Has No Spring? 230

— Luo Ailan

Brother Liewen:

Your letter asked me to write something for your esteemed publication, suggesting I use the epistolary style to describe my observations and experiences in America to enlighten readers at home. In your esteemed opinion, perhaps you think that having me talk about things from across the ocean would avoid touching any sensitive "nets." But you don't know my difficulties. If I were to write down everything I've seen and heard, I would offend many people, smash many well-established clay idols back home, and puncture many beautifully pasted paper tigers. Someone as clever as you and I wouldn't do such a foolish thing. People back home are treating overseas students like kaleidoscopes, like peep shows, holding them up to look again and again, playing with them over and over. How could we do such a spoilsport thing as tearing down the peep show?

But I can't refuse your kind intentions. I've been away from home for five years. Due to my environment and personal temperament, I've rarely picked up a pen to prattle to my compatriots. Now, my retirement fund is running low, and I have to return home. Taking advantage of this spare time, I'm reviving my writing and returning to my life with pen and ink. It's almost spring now. Since we're not to "discuss state affairs," and we can't talk about the ungentlemanly words and deeds of the old overseas students, let's talk about "Spring in New York." This belongs to the "The weather is nice today, haha" category, so I don't think it will offend anyone.

I remember once in a "Writing Workshop" class at Columbia University, a professor gave us a topic: "Spring in New York." I don't remember what I wrote at the time, but I remember the opening line: "New York has no spring."

At that time, I had been in New York for less than a year. Besides attending classes and the library, I sometimes took the subway to Times Square to see a show. I rarely went anywhere else. What I saw were tall buildings, and people and cars hurrying back and forth on the streets. I rarely had the opportunity to see the sun directly during the day, and I never dreamed of seeing the moonlight at night. When the streets were covered in snow and people were busy buying Christmas presents, I knew it was winter; when the sun during the day made me sweat and people were wearing straw hats, I knew it was summer. As for spring, I really didn't know that New York had such a thing as "spring." The same was true for autumn. So I started by writing, "New York has no spring."

That was three years ago. When you live in a place for a long time, you discover many things that you could never discover in a short period of time. You realize that you know far too little about the local customs and conditions. I remember a certain gentleman nicknamed "Terrible" passed through New York. Before his seat was even warm, he returned home and wrote a travelogue of New York, translating Fifth Avenue, a street wider and busier than Nanjing Road in Shanghai, as "Fifth Alley." I don't know how wide the alleys are in his esteemed hometown, but they can't be wider than Fifth Avenue, which divides the east and west sides of New York. As for these kinds of people, I can only admire their boldness. It is said that there are quite a few such people back home. Who says we are a cowardly nation?

If I had left New York at that time, I might have always said that New York has no spring. But I lived there for three years, and in my spare time, I explored New York in every direction. Only then did I gradually realize that New York is not without spring.

In New York, what makes you feel the arrival of spring first is the various colorful billboards. These advertisers are truly the so-called first to feel the changing trends. From the elevated trains in the sky to the subway cars underground, from the rooftops to the delivery trucks, when you no longer see the advertisements selling cold remedies, or the advertisements depicting girls who get dates with men because they use Lifebuoy soap to get rid of BO (body odor), and they shed their fur coats and change into spring clothes, you know that spring is coming to the world. (To be continued)

On "Fighting" 231

— Man

In the coastal villages of our country, a certain custom is often maintained—armed brawls. This is true not only in coastal areas but also in the interior.

Speaking of it, this is a remnant of barbarism. People from Village A and Village B often argue over a small road during the lantern festivals or competitions, refusing to give way. During the dispute, there is bound to be a fierce fight, often resulting in bloodshed, with several deaths and injuries. This is immediately followed by years of endless lawsuits, causing many people to be impoverished. And even if wise local officials are willing to help the people overcome difficulties and resolve disputes, they are often at a loss.

Why are they unwilling to give way a little? Their traditional notion is that giving way is a very unlucky thing. Of course, there may be a lot of resentment brewing between the farmers of Village A and Village B due to disputes over fields, water, and various other minor matters. When they encounter a situation with many people, they feel that the opportunity has arrived, and they must take a major revenge, so they fight. But even farmers who are at peace with each other can easily fight in such situations because giving way is "inauspicious" to them.

Scholars say: This is mob spirit! It's due to the lack of widespread education and the failure to civilize customs!…

"However, that's not the case." The burning of black slaves in America and the beating of Jews in Western Europe are not necessarily due to low levels of education. There is a fighting spirit in human nature. Even daily entertainment, gambling, and games are still interesting because they involve competition and winning or losing. "He loves bravery more than I do, but he doesn't know where to take it!" Confucius criticized Zilu in this way, but it has already been proven that Confucius himself loved bravery to an extreme. "Beyond" this extreme is of course not acceptable, so it is not worth taking.

Inauspiciousness is certainly a superstition, but there is a great deal of truth in it—it embodies the nation's vitality! Imagine if everyone in this nation said "Amitabha" and yielded in everything, becoming as soft and weak as a lump of mud. Wouldn't that be terrible? Whether it's the "people of the Land of Innocence" or the "people of the Land of Perfect Bliss," the spirit of the people will weaken, degenerate, and regress in a peaceful environment. Allowing student groups in American universities to fight, even to the point of bloodshed, without recording demerits or expelling them, is not without profound reasoning.

Moreover, brave and martial people are commendable. Only with bravery and martial spirit can one have compassion. Confucius liked those who were "zealous" because they could easily enter the "Way." Weak, effeminate, speaking of compassion but harboring resentment, is what is truly hopeless.

Life and Death (End) 232

— Zhou Lengjia

I secretly thanked her in my heart. At the same time, a trace of weariness invaded my body, and I couldn't help but yawn. I was indeed a bit exhausted. I had been in this hospital for three days, and I had hardly closed my eyes during those three days. As soon as I heard my wife's voice, my heart would jump anxiously, fearing that she was about to give birth. Now that she had given birth, my heart was relieved, and fatigue quickly took over my spirit. But I didn't want to rest or sleep. I was just worried about home. It had been three days since I had returned home. I wondered what a mess it must be in? The dust had probably filled the entire house, and the letters and publications on the table had probably piled up into a small hill. These all needed me to go back and sort them out. So, I told my wife this.

My wife didn't object. She just said, "You must come back here tonight."

"Why?" I asked her blankly.

My wife didn't speak. Her face suddenly turned red. I suddenly understood that she was just timid and didn't dare to sleep alone in the hospital. So, I comforted her with a few words and promised to come back before dark, and then I left her and took the bus home.

The situation at home was not as bad as I had imagined. The air was just a bit colder, but otherwise nothing had changed. The dust was only a thin layer on the furniture, and there were only four or five letters and publications on the table. I casually opened a letter and took a look, and couldn't help but be shocked. The letter was from my aunt's house, reporting that my cousin had passed away from illness. This news really gave me a big shock, because just four or five days ago, this cousin was still drifting around Shanghai, staying at our place. He had come to Shanghai to find a way out because he couldn't make a living in his hometown, but he didn't have any talent. In the end, he didn't find a way out and instead returned home with an illness. I deeply sympathized with his misfortune, although I was ashamed that I didn't have the power to help him. But I didn't expect him to die so quickly. How quickly people come together and separate in life! I held the letter, stood in the house, looked at the sunlight outside the window, and couldn't help but feel a little melancholy.

The world was still the same world, life was still the same life, and I was still living in this world and this life. The only difference was that I had added a child, while my cousin, whom I had seen often from childhood to the present, had turned into a foreign object.

"One soul has just been born into the world, while another soul has been forced to death by society. What kind of life is this?" I thought painfully, and a shiver ran through my entire body. A big question welled up in my mind: How can I ensure that my child will not follow in the footsteps of my cousin in the future and be reduced to a life of decline and early death?

I thought silently, but my heart felt a faint pain. I no longer regarded the birth of my child as a happy event.

In the evening, when I returned to the hospital, my wife greeted me with a smile, took the child out of the blanket for me to see, and said to me,

"I forgot to ask you, what should we name him?"

I looked at the child's little face, but I vaguely saw the shadow of my newly deceased cousin flickering before my eyes. I couldn't bless this child anymore. I forced a bitter smile and said,

"Just call him Ming'er (Tomorrow). Although he was born at dawn, it is still uncertain whether he will bring some light to this world."

To the Exile 233

— Wu He

Is it longing for the homeland beneath the white clouds? Why stand silently before the monument

all day long?

Tell me about the homeland, exile! Look,

the geese cross the sky.

Western Journey Daily Log (7) 234

— Yu Dafu

This segment of the legend is truly a palace-style short story with a great deal of poetic flavor; perhaps because it is too poetic, both the Lin'an Annals and the Yuqian Annals record this event in detail, using it for embellishment. As a result, both East Tianmu and West Tianmu have Eye-Washing Ponds, Zhaoming Temples, Prince's Palaces, and Scripture-Dividing Platforms. When writers are alive, their articles are often not worth half a penny, and they mostly starve to death. But when their flesh turns to ashes and their bones turn to charcoal, everyone wants to attach themselves to them, climbing the dragon and clinging to the phoenix, scrambling to claim association. Is this truly the permanent effect of literature? Analyzing it, I think there are still many material causes. Because when writers are alive, they still need to eat, wear clothes, and have children. But after they have died for hundreds of years, there is naturally no need for material provision. Mentioning that someone once lived here, someone once came here, can attract tourists and earn a few pennies; and monks and Taoists can use this to raise money by begging and deception, building magnificent and splendid temples and pagodas. If this is not a material cause, then what is it?

Coming out of the Lion's Mouth, after seeing the Thousand Character Rock and the Lion Rock, follow the mountain path eastward. Pass the Eye-Washing Pond, where there is a pool of water under a tree, and then go around the so-called Tree King, a giant cedar tree that takes fifteen or sixteen arm spans to encircle. After walking one or two li, you will arrive at the Upper Old Founding Hall. This stretch of road from the Lion's Mouth to the Founding Hall, which is along the mountainside, is all flat, with very many old trees and strange rocks. There are also many wide and open foundations, of which one does not know the number. The ancient temples of West Tianmu that I mentioned earlier must have been in this area. It is also possible that the Founding Hall is the Lion Progenitor Zen Temple. The plaque with the large characters "Great Tree Hall" written by Xu Shichang, hanging in the back room of the Founding Hall, presumably refers to the Tree King. In reality, there are many large trees here, and it cannot be considered a unique and rare sight. The ultimate scenery of West Tianmu, however, lies in the so-called Hanging Lotus Flower Cliff, a cliff over a hundred zhang high, standing upright like a lotus flower. Behind this lotus flower is an even more precipitous cliff, about two hundred zhang high, facing one petal of the lotus flower. Standing at the foot of the cliff and looking up, there is only a line of sky two or three chi wide, shining whitely above. Next to the Lotus Flower Rock, a few chi away, there is also a stone platform, which is flat on top and has an octagonal pavilion built on it. On the east side of the road leading to this pavilion, a cluster of strange rocks looks like the hand of a Buddha reaching towards the sky, towering at the top of a deep valley. Above this Buddha's Finger is not far from the Mountain Hall. At the top of the two rocky noses protruding south... the panoramic view of the valley seen from these two rocky noses is the only great view of West Tianmu. For the master Yutang to have arrived at West Tianmu, but not to come to this place to appreciate the panoramic view of the nearby valley, and the steep, upright cliffs and strange rocks, would be the greatest mistake in the world, the Dichung suppressing the Wahaheit!

One of the rocky noses is a unique peak that extends southward from the front of the Founding Hall for about one li, which is the place the monks call the Upside-Down Lotus Flower. Looking south from the tip of the peak, one can see the streams, villages, small mountains, and fields within several hundred li clearly. The valleys, the streams, the fields, can be likened to an upside-down fan. The fan ribs are the remaining veins branching off from West Tianmu, the white paper in between the fan ribs are the streams and villages between the veins, and the famous painting painted on this fan is an extremely delicate and meticulous brush painting with rapeseed yellow, peach blossom red, plum blossom white, mountain colors, and trees in a touch of green!

Farmhouse 235

— Lü Shaoguang

In the vast twilight,

the farmer's wife's

constant calls to the pigs rise up.

The haggard farmer,

leading a yellow ox on his back,

carrying a heavy rake,

walks wearily, like a ghost,

across the desolate field ridges.

A crescent moon, faintly

outlines the desolate thatched hut.

The yellow ox in the pen,

mourns plaintively,

awakening the farmer's illusions…

Little Mao's mother,

go quickly and see what's wrong with the ox,

I'm shivering all over again…

Mother (2) 236

— Luo Hong

Before long, the doorbell rang, and then two children rushed in, shouting,

"A guest has come!" After the older child said this, he turned around and looked at the visitor very shyly.

The father responded to the child's words and went out to greet the guest he had told the children about. After greeting the guest himself, he affectionately bent down and patted the child on the shoulder, saying,

"This is the guest I just told you about. You should all call her Auntie Li!"

The children called out shyly. The guest was a young woman, wearing a deep red cheongsam, with slightly curled hair and a long, round face with a smile, looking very gentle. She walked up to the children and gave them each a delicate and beautiful box. The younger child looked at the box for a while and said with a smile, "Daddy, it's chocolate!"

"That's right. Are you happy?"

The child looked at the smiling father and then at the smiling guest, as if thanking the guest for this satisfying gift. Afterwards, they saw their father sitting with the guest in the living room and Auntie Lu serving flowers, so the two of them retreated to the study. They were exceptionally excited to have a female guest in their home, and each of them had received a box of things they loved to eat.

"Brother, I like your box. Look, your box has red flowers, mine isn't red," the girl said, grabbing her brother's hand.

When her brother heard her say this, he seemed to think that his box was really better than hers, and he shook his head, refusing to give it up. But she kept asking, so he said,

"Then let's open them both and see if they're all chocolate!"

The candies were the same, so the younger sister stopped talking. They each ate a piece and ran to the living room. The father was talking intimately with the guest. It was rare to see the father looking so happy. Seeing them coming, the father smiled at them and said to the guest, "Let's take a look at our study!" The guest stood up, took the girl's hand, and the father walked in front, pointing out each item to the guest.

"Whenever I come home, I always work here. Look, things are so messy here, it's terrible."

The guest smiled happily and nodded. The girl always looked up at them talking and laughing. Suddenly, she remembered the mother's photo near the clothes rack, so she said to the guest coquettishly,

"There's also a photo of Mommy over there, look!"

The guest followed the direction indicated by the little hand. It was a photo of a young woman. The forceful gaze, the short hair, and the smile on the corners of her mouth showed that she had a very decisive expression. The girl continued to look at the guest, and the older brother looked at the mother's photo for a while and then looked at the guest as well. They thought that the guest would definitely praise their mother happily. But they saw the smile on the guest's face fade away. She looked at the father, patted the girl's shoulder, and said,

Yarn Exchange Announces Increased Special Margin for New Marked Yarn Sellers 245

The price drop in cotton yarn recently has become increasingly intense, with a sense of irreversible decline. The price drop in the April marked yarn is the most tragic. It was found that the price on March 15 was 185 yuan, the price of the April marked cotton was 42.3 yuan, and yesterday's closing price of marked yarn was 160.03 yuan, a drop of 24.7 yuan, and the marked cotton was 41.4 yuan, a drop of only 0.9 yuan. The price difference between yarn and cotton is getting farther and farther apart, which shows the difficulties of the factory. It was found that the reasons for the decline in cotton yarn are: 1. The decline in rural areas and the depression of sales, resulting in an increase in inventory; 2. Although the factories have repeatedly convened meetings, ostensibly sympathizing with the proposal that each yarn should not be sent to the exchange, it is contrary to the facts. The amount of each yarn in the warehouse is increasing day by day, and opinions are still difficult to unify. Therefore, speculators regard the abundant chips in the exchange, and the Bao Feng suddenly rises, and the Japanese merchants sell even more enthusiastically. As a result, the entire yarn market has been broken, resulting in a sharp decline. The current market situation is estimated to be difficult to maintain at the 60 yuan level. Therefore, yesterday, the factory party requested that the exchange increase the special margin of 8 yuan in cash for each bale of new sales for each month's term of marked yarn in the current week, and temporarily suppress the selling and save the yarn market. The market announcement is recorded on the left:

The Shanghai Yarn and Cloth Exchange, starting from April 19, will increase the special margin for new sales of cotton yarn in each month's term, 8 yuan in cash per bale, and the seller of each new two-stock account will also increase the special margin of 8 yuan in cash per bale. Unveiling the announcement.

Grain Rumors Unfavorable to Forward Flour, Prices Loosen and Fall 248

Yesterday, after the opening of the flour market in the morning, the market for all months generally showed a flat and weak trend. The quoted prices for foreign wheat from Chicago were down by 2.5 cents, and those from Canada were down by about 0.25 cents. At the opening, both buyers and sellers in the market were mostly in a wait-and-see attitude, and actual sales were also mostly stagnant. Some factories were engaging in near-end buying and far-end selling, while others were secretly making slight sales. Therefore, the market sentiment was already weakening amidst the fluctuations. By the time the market opened in the afternoon, rumors circulated that foreign flour and wheat would flood the market during the new wheat season, coupled with the low prices of various coarse grains, which were rare in the past decade or so. As a result, people's minds were unsettled, and prices gradually fell. Purchases from various regions had completely disappeared, which was the reason for this. This situation was already widespread, so there was probably no good prospect in the near term. Although the daily decline seemed insignificant, the prices for June and July were already on the verge of breaking through the two-dollar mark, and the unfavorable situation could be imagined. As a result, the current month was down by 0.75 cents, May was down by 0.5 cents, June was down by 1 cent, July was down by 1.125 cents, August was down by 0.5 cents, and September was down by 1 cent.

Forward Wheat Sales Sentiment Relatively Strong 249

Yesterday, the forward wheat market showed a weak trend in all months after the opening in the morning and afternoon. The quoted prices for foreign wheat from Chicago were down by 2.5 cents, and those from Canada were down by about 0.25 cents. After the opening in the morning, the price for the current month was down sharply by 0.7 cents compared to the opening price earlier in the week because it had not opened for several days and there was a surge of arrivals. Later, it did not open. The prices for distant months were relatively stable because of the slight rain in the morning. By the afternoon, the weather had cleared up, and the sales sentiment for June, July, and August became strong, and people's minds became even more unsettled. The opening prices gradually loosened. According to the industry insiders' prediction, the old standard would have to reach 0.3 dollars, and the new standard would have to reach between 0.4 and 0.5 dollars, because the goods from the countryside would inevitably flood the market during the new crop season. As a result, June was down by 0.3 cents, July remained unchanged, and August was down by 0.2 cents. There was no delivery of spot wheat because factory stomachs were temporarily suspended.

Silk and Tea: Zhejiang's Spring Silkworms Affected by Cold Weather 255

(Uneven Hatching, Delayed Development) In "Huzhou," improved varieties are not hatching well, and silkworm rearing has been delayed due to cold weather. Young silkworms are shivering and afraid of the cold, so fire is used to warm them, which is not good for their development. Early batches have been feeding leaves for six or seven days since their first sleep, while late batches have just started feeding leaves. In "Yuhang," the early silkworm eggs hatched by farmers have all been delayed in hatching, and most have been used to raise late silkworms. The amount raised is only 50-60% of last year. The early batches will soon have completed their first sleep, but their development is not healthy. In "Xucun," silkworm farmers are all raising improved varieties this year. Although the hatching was earlier than last year, silkworm rearing was delayed. Mulberry buds are also developing slowly due to cold weather. Early silkworms are feeding leaves for two sleeps, while late silkworms have been feeding leaves for five or six days since their first sleep.

(New York Raw Silk Prices Continue to Fall) In the New York raw silk market, raw silk prices continue to fall. Silk weaving factories are focusing on rayon for summer silks, so the demand for raw silk is weak. Japanese silk is being dumped at low prices. The price of standard Japanese silk is only $1.245 per pound, which is equivalent to a drop of nearly $400 per bale in Chinese currency. Chinese silk in hand is also being sold at discounted prices. B-grade white filature silk with a uniformity of 78-80% is only being offered at $500, but there are few buyers.

(Sichuan Yellow Native Silk Continues to Be Shipped to Shanghai) Yesterday, the Minsheng steamer arrived in Shanghai from Hankou and loaded 25 pieces of Sichuan yellow native silk, which were taken back by the Sichuan silk stores to be sold.

(Shanghai Silk Sales Quiet and Dull) Overseas silk weaving factories have weak demand for raw silk, and raw silk prices continue to decline. Japanese silk dumping is still strong, and no one is inquiring about Chinese silk. Shanghai manufacturers are pledging their silk stocks and preparing to close down. Silk sales are quiet. Yesterday, only Xinfu imported 10 bales of gray filature silk, and Chouqi imported 5 bales of yellow filature silk, both at weakening prices.

Hangzhou New Tea Has Started to Be Weighed 256

Hangzhou green tea has always been the earliest to come out each year, but this year, due to the cold weather, tea buds have not been easy to develop. Therefore, since Qingming, most mountains have not yet started picking. According to a letter from Hangzhou, new Longjing tea from West Lake has already been launched on the market. However, due to the small amount of production and the high demand from Shanghai and Hangzhou buyers, the opening price for the first lot is 665 yuan per dan. In addition, tea farmers on Lion Peak have also begun picking tea, and a large number of new goods should be launched on the market within days.

Wuyuan Tea Industry Declining 257

Wuyuan is an important tea-producing area. Every year, it produces and sells no less than 70,000 boxes of foreign-style green tea. Since Tunxi and Shexian began to compete in the production of needle-shaped Zhenmei, the tea industry in this area has been greatly affected. Although the accounts were settled last year with varying degrees of profit and loss, the local vitality has weakened to the extreme. In addition, tea loans are still tight, so most tea houses are hesitant to act. As the new tea is about to arrive on the market, more than 20 tea houses have announced their closure, and others are also reducing their scale. The tea industry in this area is gradually showing a declining trend.

Piece Goods: Demand for Valeting Exceeds Supply 258

Valeting is even more popular this year, and sales of Western-style clothing are particularly strong. Although the peak sales season has not yet arrived, the industry has already begun to search for supplies. It is heard that three boxes arrived yesterday from Shanghai No. 2 and were immediately sold out, with prices ranging from $5.25 to $5.50 per yard. Those who did not obtain any are sighing with regret. It is estimated that the cost per yard is about $3.90.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Commentary

The North China Crisis 259

— Gu She

Since the September 18th Incident, North China has been in a very serious crisis. This crisis reached an unprecedented level of tension in the months before the signing of the Tanggu Truce last year. After the signing of the Tanggu Truce, the North China crisis, although temporarily eased slightly, continued to develop in secret. The delay in returning the war zone, the difficulty of bandit suppression, the continuous appearance of puppet troops, the occupation of Dolon, the emergency in Chahar and Suiyuan, and the occasional reconnaissance flights of Japanese aircraft over the outskirts of Peiping have all kept the entire North China in a state of anxiety and shock. North of the Yellow River, there has hardly been a moment of peace and stability since the September 18th Incident.

Japan's invasion of China is very methodical. Before the September 18th Incident, when the world economic panic was developing to its deepest level, the economies and politics of various countries were very turbulent and uneasy. It anticipated that when this bomb exploded, the countries would be too busy to take care of themselves, and there would be no way to intervene. Sure enough, when the September 18th Incident broke out, it only added some turmoil to world politics, but no one dared to say that Japan was wrong in its actions, and some even secretly helped. Japan had anticipated this move.

After Japan occupied Northeast China, on the one hand, it dealt with the world, and most importantly, on the other hand, it also had to deal with the Chinese people, because the Chinese people are anti-imperialist and anti-Japanese. At this time, all his energy was focused on dealing with China. If China dared not move or make a sound again, then it would be easy for him to talk to the world. After considerable effort, China did not dare to move or make a sound again. Japan's goal was achieved as desired.

After China's submission, Japan still had to work hard with the world to change the attitude of the world powers towards Japan's actions from opposition to approval, or at least indifference, and then further recognize the puppet state. This is what Japan has been striving for. Naturally, the result has been quite successful. Although the recognition of the puppet state is not yet so fast, the attitude of indifference has been achieved.

However, China has in fact submitted, but it has not yet recognized the puppet state. Secondly, the existence of the Soviet Union is also a major annoyance to the development of Japanese imperialism. How can China be made to move from factual submission to simply recognizing the puppet state? How to drive the Soviet Union away so that it can develop without hindrance? This is what Japan is currently racking its brains to plan and deal with. And the current tension in North China and the deepening of the North China crisis day by day are precisely the manifestation of this plan of Japan.

Japan's control of North China by force, making it impossible for North China to have a moment of peace, while at the same time peeking into Chahar and Suiyuan, is aimed at: 1. Forcing our country to recognize the puppet state and conducting direct negotiations under the coercion of force; 2. Challenging the Soviet Union and forcing the Soviet Union to retreat. In addition, treating North China in the same way as it treated the Eastern Provinces in the past, secretly controlling the economic and political lifeline of North China, and when the time is right, it will further occupy North China north of the Yellow River. This is the origin of the deepening North China crisis.

The Eastern Provinces have been lost, and North China is under the control of Japanese military force. In the near future, Japan will inevitably further take North China in the same way that it took the Eastern Provinces. After North China succeeds, it will then further peer into Central and South China. Although it is another question whether Japan will have more violent conflicts with Britain, the United States, and other countries at that time, in short, Japan's predetermined goal is this. The people of the country should remember that they should not think that local submission can be exchanged for Japan's permanent peace. It must be known that this is a definite step-by-step process for its invasion of China. Its ultimate goal is the whole of China!

Freedom of Occupation and Marriage and Social Relations 260

— Jia Wei

If we were to statistically analyze all the suicide incidents in society, then the results obtained would be… perhaps more than half would be due to economic oppression—unemployment, no way out—and the lack of freedom in marriage! We can definitely say this. Indeed, a lot of participants' energy, various colors of ink, and the pages of various newspapers have been spent discussing and researching these two personal problems of modern youth - occupation and marriage; but in fact, because of such incidents, they are still circulating like deeply rooted ones in all strata of society, increasing rather than decreasing and not getting the slightest solution. Therefore, in general, scholars who are bored and insensitive, if they hear about this kind of problem, they will appear to be overwhelmed and annoyed, because they have long regarded it as "old news." But the facts have not told us that this problem cannot be so simple.

Originally, the problem of occupation and marriage is not a simple isolated problem. They have a close relationship with the entire society, and this is seen and admitted by everyone except those who are willing to only consult the "one-sided" for a lifetime. Moreover, in the past historical process of mankind, it has already indicated to us that… a society, in an era and under a system, has its different kinds of social phenomena and the sum of its key relationships; and in a different society, all kinds of spiritual relationships——general social phenomena——are determined and dominated by its material economic relations. Well, since we have recognized these realistic and objective conditions… occupation and marriage must be governed by objective material conditions, then it is not difficult for us to understand the so-called freedom of occupation and marriage in the current stage of society.

Various capitalist powers have a direct relationship with China, and this is something that no one would deny, right? Therefore, if we want to understand our society today, we must also know them. Isn't it already early? In all aspects, it can be seen that… within the various capitalist countries, and on the world stage of mutual struggle among the various imperialist countries, all the contradictions of the capitalist system have been deepened and sharpened to the greatest extent. This is what has made the entire national economy of various capitalist countries "periodic," "sudden," and constantly declining. Due to this capitalist widespread panic, a powerful "world economic panic" was generated, which shocked and agitated every corner of the world.

Our China, of course, is not qualified to become a capitalist country, but it has always become a large market for free competition among various capitalist powers… In this way, our originally unsound and mixed economic organization, under the agitation of this great wave of the "world economic panic," can only "doubly" follow them—the widespread panic of capitalism—and decline, decline! At the same time, the strengthening of the distance between the various strata of society has undoubtedly become a "direct proportion." Look! The great collapse of the entire rural economy, the bankruptcy, decline, and collapse of the middle class—small merchants, small farmers, salaried workers, etc.—have caused a shocking surge in the number of unemployed and all kinds of social pathologies… factory and shop closures, labor-management disputes, sharp increases in prisoners, suicides… are all alarming and sad facts that arise in response to the times!

Enough, these phenomena are enough to give us extremely clear instructions; in this "doubly" declining current stage, "survival of the fittest" is the main condition, competition, struggle, exclusion... are the most personal skills. In this way, to want "freedom" in occupation today, of course, there is no way to talk about it. But there are exceptions, and that is only because in this social and economic organization, economics is the supreme authority, so only by getting help from it can we have "freedom" today! As for the problem of freedom of marriage, this magazine has discussed it a lot, and its conclusion is… in today's everything is commodified, this—marriage autonomy and the free love of preconditions—is of course no exception, so this is nothing more than the "patent" of the rich, and at the same time it is just the free competition of money and incense powder exchange and buying and selling! In short… it cannot escape the domination of the social environment! The reason why every problem becomes "old news" is because it is "always talking about old news," right—"always" talked about by people and still "old" is "existing"—in this way, it clearly tells us that this kind of problem cannot be solved just by talking about it on the mouth or on paper. Young friends! Now, only by relying on yourselves, according to the "route" and instructions that have come down from the historical process, recognizing all the "realities" that are constantly developing today, to determine your own "trend" and assume the proper "mandate," can you obtain the true "freedom" that you need!

The Spring Scenery is Good 261

— Meng Jun

Leaning on my cane, I lengthened my gaze and looked out over the distance. A large patch of red clouds resting on the treetops immediately reminded me of the two sentences I had copied when my teacher ordered me to write a spring outing record when I was a child as a descriptive language: "The fragrant grass is fresh and beautiful, and the fallen flowers are colorful."

I have no feelings, let alone any thoughts! In fact, there is no room for these! At this moment, I tried my best to abandon the old thoughts accumulated in my brain and let these fresh elements of life really nourish me. A gloomy young man should no longer cling to the things that have passed away. If he does not want to look forward to the future emptily, he must at least really enjoy the present minute, second, and even flash.

"When facing the wine, sing aloud, how much of life is there? Like the morning dew, there are not many days left." Friends, is this life, like the morning dew, to be missed lightly? The past has left you ruthlessly; the future is vague.

"Only nature is infinitely rich," I said repeatedly as I walked. People on the main road brushed past me in twos and threes. I didn't bother to look at them, but the voices of their easy conversations often reached my ears, always giving me a different feeling than in the past… the world is not all cold and terrible.

My body moved forward leisurely with my footsteps. Finally, I stopped by a ditch. The water flowing in the ditch, of course, cannot be compared with the gurgling spring water, but the clarity of the water may not necessarily be inferior to the spring water. However, spring water is admired, while ditch water is despised, which really makes me feel something. Yes, ditch water is ordinary, just irrigating… spring water, on the other hand, is not. This is Hupao, this is the No. 1 spring in the world. A generation of men of letters with leisure and elegance are willing to spend their precious ink to write a grand stroke and inscribe such elegant names; as for ditch water, people almost don't bother to look at it. What I don't understand is… apart from the surface having a peculiar interest, what else does spring water actually have? The reason why spring water is admired is probably because of its appearance. ——This can really show the general state of the world, emphasizing appearance and neglecting content. It is like this for things, and why should people treat it differently?

I stared into the ditch and saw countless tadpoles burrowing against the mud on both sides of the water. Balls of small black animals floated in my eyes for a moment without stopping. Isn't this ball of small animals the most appropriate microcosm of human beings? —Unconsciously busy seeking survival, but eventually dying, generation after generation, without interruption.

The heat of the sun penetrated my clothes and made my back abnormally hot. I had turned from the main road onto a field bank just wide enough for one person to walk. Looking at a glance, the dense peach trees were lined up in front of me like infinite people. At this moment, I no longer wanted to imagine anything else, and I just basked in this atmosphere here!

Suddenly, a burst of singing came from the peach forest. Obviously, it was a duet…

The eight-piece skirt flutters in the wind, and the little sister's wedding date will arrive in the blink of an eye; I'm not used to strangers everywhere, dear brother, what do you think is good? … … … … … … … … … … The eight-piece skirt flutters in the wind, how can I bear my little sister marrying someone else? Let's pack our bags and leave together, you and I will grow old together.

The Story of a Street Urchin (24) 262

— Made by Chen Jingsheng

"Reporting to the General, we're going to the front line!" The gramophone stolen in a mischievous prank became a good friend in the trenches.

The Flower-Selling Girl 263

— Rose

Women, from the moment they are born, possess a bewitching allure. That fair skin, those cherry lips, that graceful figure—since ancient times, they have intoxicated countless men. And that voice is also enchanting enough.

"Gardenia, White Orchid!"

It is a clear and moving voice, like a mechanical alarm clock, that awakens me from my dreams every morning at a fixed time.

"Gardenia, White Orchid," one cry follows another, sung from one end of the alley to the other, like a melody containing a charming rhythm. This melody is sung year-round in the early morning, only changing with the seasons. Sometimes it sings of "roses," sometimes of "hydrangeas," sometimes of "tuberose," sometimes of "chrysanthemums," sometimes of "wintersweet," and sometimes of "narcissus." But the melody is always the same, using the same rhythm, sung in the quiet early morning.

Sometimes I seem to dream of a strange realm, a beautiful celestial music vibrating in the air. Then, I would habitually feel as if some force was urging me, and I would struggle to open my eyes. A very careful, low knock would come from the door, followed by another charming and clear cry, "Sir, would you like white orchids?"

I had grown accustomed to hearing this rhythm, accustomed to experiencing this scene. The flower-selling girl had also become accustomed to walking into my door. Every day she walked into my door, every day she brought me fresh flowers, and every day she gave me a deeper impression. And so we became familiar with each other.

She was still an innocent girl, only fifteen years old, but she already had a job and was making a living for herself! From spring to summer, from autumn to winter, every morning she used the same clear voice to peddle flowers. This was her profession, yet her clear voice was even more moving than the flowers, arousing people's pity.

One day last week, I woke up at the usual time, but the rhythm of the flower-selling girl that I was accustomed to hearing was silent. I waited and waited, but the image I was accustomed to seeing no longer appeared before my eyes. Thus, every morning when I woke up, I would feel disappointed, as if I had lost something. Every day I waited for that lost thing to return, but every day I was disappointed.

Today, I woke up again at the usual time—it seemed as if that same rhythm was coming from the alley! I excitedly hoped for that careful, low sound... but it came... sang from one end of the alley to the other, but did not sing to my door. So, I got out of bed again in disappointment, opened the window, and looked towards the place where the rhythm was coming from. But it was no longer the image I was accustomed to seeing. It was an elderly woman and an even younger girl. So, under the pretext of buying flowers, I called them over and casually inquired about the previous flower-selling girl. It turned out that the elderly woman was her mother, and the younger girl was her younger sister. And what about her? She had caught the eye of the master in the Wang mansion and was going to be a concubine.

"Isn't she still very young?" I asked. "That's precisely why someone wants her, because she's young! Like me, my age is almost the same as my son-in-law, but I'm old, who wants me?... But my daughter isn't that young anymore, she'll be sixteen next year!... Now I'm bringing this younger daughter out to sell flowers, she's only eight years old!"

"Hmm, women, are just like flowers, you have to pick the ones that are just budding. Women, are valuable only in their youth. 'Old, who wants them?'" I murmured to myself.

Amateur Mailbox

Further on the Marriage Problem 264

Editor Sir:

I am now twenty-four years old, and my parents will be marrying me off at the end of this year. Originally, I was betrothed when I was around ten years old. In the years 1929 or 1930, that never-before-seen fiancée of mine unfortunately died of illness, which I didn't particularly mind. But my mother regretted it. I thought that from then on, I could choose my own wife. I even declared to my parents that they shouldn't bother on my behalf in the future. However, no matter how much you spend your breath, they won't listen to you.

In the early summer of 1931, they actually carried out the betrothal ceremony without even notifying me. When I was still studying at a school in Shanghai, I returned home for summer vacation and learned of this, but there was no way to reverse it. After the fact, I heard about the process of this matter and the background of the other party. Initially, the other party was a tenant of my aunt's family, and they naturally became familiar and close through daily meetings. My mother took a liking to that daughter because of her gentle and quiet nature, and also because she had the skill of knitting socks. My father, on the other hand, was rather careless and never gave a definite expression of approval. So, the completion of the matter was entirely due to my mother's opinion alone. Her family was originally in the city of Wuxi, but they moved to our town after losing their jobs. The entire family's living expenses depended on the income from the two daughters' knitting socks. The elder daughter was already married, so life became even more difficult. It was already difficult to barely maintain their livelihood, let alone educate their daughters.

Since then, there have been several disputes within the family, and I have shed many bitter tears. My reasons for resisting are that there is no basis in mutual love, and that the other party is illiterate. Many of my friends have advised me not to resist this matter, and have even explained it to me. If she is illiterate, you can teach her after marriage, and she may be able to write letters and read books. They even congratulated me, saying that I would have a financially independent wife.

I have gone through many troubles over this matter. Should I compromise? Or should I refuse? Whenever a stimulus to move forward comes, I will strive to arouse a rebellious mentality. But whenever I encounter some discouragement, I will be like a sheep, justifying myself and thinking that there is no need to cause trouble. Sometimes,

Page 21

Page 22

Page 23

I feel that resistance is powerless, and I think of not interfering in this matter. What worries me the most is that since then, the fire of youth seems to have been extinguished, all ambitions have been dispelled, and I dare not even think about courageous thoughts anymore. I believe that if it is already like this before marriage, how much more lifeless and destructive it will be after marriage. If I compromise, I know that I will be tightly bound, with no chance of turning over, and I fear that I will end my life silently and without spirit. Although after resisting, what will happen in the end is still unknown, I am certain that resistance will lead to a breakdown in the emotional relationship between parents and children, and will hurt their old hearts. As for indifference, I know that things will eventually explode one day and cannot be escaped. So, the question now is whether I should follow my heart and compromise, or respect my own wishes and resist?

If I resist, then the one hundred yuan betrothal gift will naturally not be returned, and whether the other party may have reasons to refuse to dissolve the engagement and how I will appease the anger of the elders, and how I will comfort their pain.

I know very well that the main reason my mother is marrying me off is to relieve her of her responsibilities, and at the same time to gain someone to help manage the household affairs. As for me, I may not be satisfied. This kind of behavior of abandoning one's wife at home and letting her live a lonely life is unkind. Other problems may be put aside, but I cannot teach her to read. First, I have my own affairs, so I have no spare time. Second, whether she has the energy to learn is also a question. So, if I am to compromise, my mental suffering goes without saying, and as for my career, not only is there no hope of help, but there is even the hatred of obstruction. Guo Sumin replies: This letter was forwarded by the Reading Guidance Department of the newspaper's circulation library. Mr. Guo's situation is extremely common. It is a problem that should exist in this society of rapid transition between the old and the new.

Of course, the union of men and women should be based on love, and marriage should be autonomous. But the editor has said before that although marriage is a lifelong event, it is not the only thing in life. A happy marriage is of course a lifelong happiness, but an unhappy marriage does not mean that all happiness is lost. Therefore, young people in general should be very careful about marriage and should not be careless in the slightest. That is indeed right, but if one puts one's whole mind on the issue of a spouse, it seems to be taking too narrow a view of life.

We believe that marriage is like eating, although it is indispensable, it has no great significance. Therefore, we do not want young people in general to create the motto "living for marriage or love." Therefore, we believe that as long as a spouse does not hinder the career you wish to pursue, and you can get along peacefully, even if their appearance and talent are somewhat inferior, it does not mean that your life will have any regrets. Therefore, your great dissatisfaction with the marriage arranged for you by your mother seems to be too deeply prejudiced. You must know that if you fall in love with a very modern girl now, you will of course feel very happy at the time, but if your material conditions are not sufficient to support her, this happiness may not last forever, and there may be days when you regret it repeatedly. Of course, this cannot be generalized. Modern girls certainly can be hardworking, but they are ultimately in the minority. Therefore, the editor believes that you should not blindly oppose the marriage arranged by your family, but you should see what the other party is like and whether you can get along peacefully in the future. Illiteracy is indeed a flaw, but not being sensible is even more harmful. If she is illiterate but still compatible with you, it does not mean that you cannot marry. Therefore, the editor believes that what you should do now is to try your best to get closer to the other party and observe her character. If you feel that there is no major conflict between her and you, then insisting on breaking off the engagement can be said to be completely unreasonable. However, after further observation, you must completely change the attitude you have adopted in this letter. You should judge based on whether your personalities and interests are close, but you should not use talent, appearance, and learning as standards.

After this careful consideration, then firmly talk about marriage or breaking off the engagement. There is no need to shed bitter tears now, and there is no need to be depressed.

Novel

Between Flesh and Blood (7) 266

— Manzhi

It seemed the servant girl came to say, the Sixth Master asks you to go quickly. The Madam immediately rose and headed toward the new house. Upon entering that flower hall, she saw the Master holding a long strip of cloth, tied into a knot and looped around their eldest son's neck who lay sprawled out on the bed. He held one end himself, and gave the other to her, saying, "Here, pull harder!" The Madam uncontrollably grasped it. The Sixth Master tugged forcefully, the Madam's head swam and her heart leaped, so she didn't pull very hard. Their eldest son's head and body were dragged to one side, and he suddenly moved the cloth strip with both hands, taking the opportunity to flip himself up and push the Master to the ground, the Madam also falling. He produced a pistol from his side, and aimed at the Master's chest, firing! The Sixth Master's chest bore a hole, red blood gushing forth! The Madam lunged forward to embrace the Sixth Master, weeping loudly. He pointed at the Master, cursing loudly, "You refuse to recognize me as your son, and I refuse to recognize you as my father! If you try to strangle me, I'll shoot you dead! Mother, get up, he brought it on himself, ignore him, let's go!" Upon hearing these words, the Madam was furious, bellowing, "It's no crime for a father to kill his son, but for a son to kill his father, you unfilial and unprincipled wretch, you lawless brute!" As the Madam spoke, she meant to fight him to the death, but she heard a loud bang, and he fired! The Madam felt a pain in her chest, and with a loud cry—she woke up! It turned out it was a nightmare. She was drenched in sweat, her chest still aching. Outside the window, a torrential rain pattered down. The Madam sat up, pondering the dream, "If you don't kill him, he'll kill you! He even shot me, that beast!" The Sixth Master lay stiff on the ground, blood gushing from his chest—that image faded and reappeared in her mind, and the more she thought about it, the more frightened she became, so the Madam lay back down on the bed, covering herself with the sheets to sleep.

Three

The next day. At dusk, Jian Guang was bored and alone in the new house, leaning against the door of the flower hall, staring blankly at the darkening sky and the drizzling rain. Pu Ning, that old bastard, led Lian Sun and Gui Sun in. Jian Guang was startled, retreating into the door. When she saw that there was no one else behind them, she was relieved. Lian Sun spoke first, "Where's Number One off to?"

"He's back, all better now," Gui Sun added.

The tone of their voices didn't seem to harbor any ill intentions, so Jian Guang hastily offered them seats, saying, "Isn't he just wandering about everywhere?" Pu Ning struck a match to light the lamp, and Jian Guang turned to them, asking, "Business good?"

Lian Sun said, "Gui Sun's made a fortune, the tax on foreign sugar went up, so Chaozhou sugar's raking in the money."

Gui Sun said, "He's the one making a fortune, passing off Japanese cloth as Hong Kong cloth, making thousands on a single batch, right?"

Jian Guang smiled slightly and said, "The newspapers are trumpeting about boycotting inferior goods and cutting off economic ties. I said that the merchants in Shantou would get rich again, for sure. What do merchants care about being patriotic? They're actually traitors, selling China to the powers for division, enthusiastic..."
